Throwing Seven Stones at Once: Hanafi vs. Three Imams
Ruling on throwing seven stones simultaneously and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing multiple stones at once, identify the condition for validity, and evaluate the opposing evidence from the three Imams.

Core Idea
Hanafi school permits a combined throw if stones spread; others require seven separate throws.

During the Hajj ritual of ramy al-jamarat, pilgrims throw seven pebbles at the jamrah. But what if a pilgrim throws all seven at once? Does it count as one throw or seven? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanbali schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that throwing seven stones at once counts as one throw, provided the stones land on different spots of the jamrah. If they land on one spot, the throw is invalid.
The condition of 'distinct actions' (tafarruq al-af'al) is key.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The three Imams (Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad) rule that it only counts as one pebble, regardless of where the stones land. They require seven separate throws.
Their evidence: the command is to throw seven times.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent's dalil is the apparent meaning of the command to perform ramy seven times, implying seven distinct acts. They do not accept the Hanafi interpretation of the number seven as preventing deficiency.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the sacred texts require distinct actions in outcome (tafarruq al-af'al), not necessarily separate lifts. The number seven is to ensure sufficiency, not to forbid combining. They analogize with combining lashes in a hadd punishment in one stroke.
Hanafi response uses both textual reasoning and qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow a combined throw if stones spread (counts as one throw, so the pilgrim must still complete six more separate throws), while the other schools require seven entirely separate throws, making the combined throw invalid except for one stone.
This affects ease for elderly or weak pilgrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله «كحصى الخذف» إلى أنه لو رمي بسبع حصيات جملة واحدة فإنه يكون عن واحدة لأن المنصوص عليه تفرق الأفعال والتقييد بالسبع لمنع النقص لا لمنع الزيادة فإنه لو رماها بأكثر من السبع لم يضره. وفي الكرماني : إذا وقعت متفرقة على مواضع الجمرات جاز كما لو جمع بين أسواط الحد بضربة واحدة وإن وقعت على مكان واحد لا يجوز. وقال مالك والشافعي وأحمد لا يجزئه إلا عن حصاة واحدة كيفما كان لأنه مأمور بالرمي سبع مرات (شرح اللباب) ثم نقل عن مصنف اللباب في منسكه الكبير أن الذي في المشاهير من كتب أصحابنا الإطلاق في عدم الجواز كما هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة، ثم نازعه بما فيه نظر لمن أحسن النظر فراجعه وتبصر.
He indicated by his saying 'like pebbles of khidhf' that if he throws seven pebbles all at once, it counts as one because the texts specify distinct actions, and the restriction to seven is to prevent deficiency, not to prevent excess; for if he throws more than seven, it does not harm him. And in al-Karmani: If they fall separately on the places of the jamarat, it is permissible, just as if one combines lashes of a hadd punishment with one stroke; but if they fall on one place, it is not permissible. Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad said: It does not suffice except for one pebble no matter how it is, because he is commanded to throw seven times. Then he narrated from the author of al-Lubab in his great ritual manual that what is well-known in our school's books is the absolute non-permissibility, just as the three Imams say. Then he disputed it with what requires consideration for the good observer; refer to it and reflect.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and the other three schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) on the ruling of throwing seven stones simultaneously. The Hanafi position, indicated by the author's commentary on the matn phrase 'كحصى الخذف', is that if a pilgrim throws seven stones all at once, it counts as only one throw. The basis is that the sacred texts (المنصوص عليه) require distinct actions (تفرق الأفعال), and the number seven serves to prevent deficiency, not to require exactly seven separate throws. Therefore, throwing extra is not harmful. The Hanafi school further elaborates through al-Karmani that if the stones land on different spots of the jamrah, the throw is valid by analogy with combining lashings for a hadd punishment in one stroke; but if all land on one spot, it is invalid. The opposing Imams argue that it only counts as one stone because the command is to throw seven separate times. The author then notes that the famous view in the Hanafi school is actually non-permissibility, agreeing with the three Imams, but this is contested. The student is advised to examine the issue carefully.

Key Terms
كحصى الخذف (ka-hasa al-khidhf): Pebbles like those used in khidhf (a type of throwing), indicating small size.
تفرق الأفعال (tafarruq al-af'al): Distinct actions; the acts should be separately executed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a pilgrim throws seven stones at once and they all land on the same spot?
A) The throw counts as seven valid throws.
B) The throw counts as one valid throw.
C) The throw is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It depends on the pilgrim's intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a combined throw for ramy al-jamarat only if the stones spread across the jamrah; otherwise it is invalid.

The Ruling on Throwing More Than Seven Stones: Intentional vs Unintentional Excess
Intra-Hanafi dispute on throwing extra stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing more than seven stones and distinguish between intentional and unintentional excess.

Core Idea
Intentional excess is disliked; unintentional is harmless.

The act of throwing stones at the jamarat has a prescribed number of seven per jamrah. What happens if one throws more? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling, resolving an apparent contradiction and presenting an intra-Hanafi dispute. The key distinction is intention: intentional excess is makruh tanzih, while unintentional excess incurs no harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The passage deals with throwing more than seven stones at a single jamrah. What is the default ruling?
The basic act is ramy al-jamarat with seven stones.
2
Note the initial statement
The matn states that throwing more than seven 'does not harm him'. This suggests the act is valid.
This is a literal reading of the text.
3
Recognize the clarification from al-Lubab
Al-Lubab and its commentator explain that it is disliked (makruh) if intentional; unintentional excess (e.g., due to doubt) is harmless.
The apparent contradiction with al-Kabir is resolved by distinguishing intention.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute and the relied-upon position
Some scholars did not dislike it, arguing throwing is obedience. The majority, including Shams al-A'imma and al-Qadi Uyayd, hold it is disliked because it goes against the sunna. The latter is the mufta bihi.
This applies a fortiori to the two jamarat on the second day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإنه لو رماها بأكثر من السبع لم يضره) قال في اللباب : ولو رمى أكثر من سبع يكره. وقال شارحه : أي إذا رماه عن قصد، وأما إذا شك في السابع ورماه وتبين أنه الثامن فإنه لا يضره ذلك. هذا وقد ناقضه في الكبير بقوله : ولو رمى بأكثر من السبع لا يضره ا هـ . أقول : ما ذكره في المنسك الكبير هو ما ذكره المؤلف هنا ولعله محمول على غير القصد فلا تناقض إذ لا شك أن السبع هو المسنون ف الزيادة عليها مخالفة للسنة فتكره لو كانت مقصودة وإلا فلا. وفي حاشية المدني قال الشيخ عز الدين بن جماعة في مناسكه الكبرى قالوا : لو زاد الرمي على السبع هل يندب أو يكره ؟ فقال بعضهم : إنه لا تكره الزيادة لأن رمیه طاعة، وقال بعضهم بل تكره لأنه خلاف السنة. هكذا نقل الخلاف ا هـ . وقال شمس الأئمة: لو زاد على سبع حصيات لا أجر له وينبغي أن يكره. قال القاضي عيد: وينبغي أن يكون هذا هو المذهب، ويكره رمي الجمرتين كذلك في هذا اليوم بالطريق الأولى لأنه بدعة ولم يفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام وربما اتخذها الجهال نسكاً ا هـ
His saying: 'For if he throws more than seven, it does not harm him.' Al-Lubab said: If he throws more than seven, it is disliked. Its commentator said: That is if he throws intentionally; whereas if he doubts the seventh and throws, and it becomes clear that it was the eighth, then that does not harm him. This has been contradicted in al-Kabir by his saying: 'If he throws more than seven, it does not harm him.' I say: What he mentioned in al-Mansak al-Kabir is what the author mentions here, and perhaps it is interpreted as unintentional, so there is no contradiction, since undoubtedly seven is the sunna, and exceeding it is contrary to the sunna, so it is disliked if intentional, otherwise not. In the marginalia of al-Madani, Shaykh Izz al-Din ibn Jama'a said in his great ritual manual: They said: If one increases the throwing beyond seven, is it recommended or disliked? Some said it is not disliked because his throwing is obedience; some said it is disliked because it is contrary to the sunna. Thus the difference is transmitted. Shams al-A'imma said: If he exceeds seven pebbles, he has no reward, and it should be disliked. Al-Qadi Uyayd said: This should be the madhhab; and it is disliked to throw the two jamarat likewise on this day, a fortiori, because it is innovation and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do it, and the ignorant might take it as a ritual.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on throwing more than seven stones at a jamrah. The initial statement from the matn says that throwing extra stones does not harm, but the commentary from al-Lubab clarifies that it is disliked (makruh) if done intentionally. The commentator resolves an apparent contradiction: if the extra throw was unintentional (e.g., due to doubt about the count), it is harmless. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion: some scholars say extra throwing is not disliked because it is still an act of obedience; others say it is disliked because it goes against the sunna. The relied-upon position (madhhab) according to Shams al-A'imma and al-Qadi Uyayd is that it is disliked. This applies even more strongly to throwing the two jamarat (on the second day) because it is an innovation. The heretical practice of the ignorant taking it as a ritual is warned against. The key distinction is between intentional and unintentional excess: intentional excess is disapproved; unintentional is excused.

Key Terms
المسنون (al-masnun): The prescribed number (seven) according to the sunna.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on intentionally throwing eight stones at the jamrah?
A) It is forbidden (haram).
B) It is permissible without any dislike.
C) It is disliked (makruh tanzih).
D) The throw is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that intentionally throwing more than seven stones is disliked (makruh tanzih), and unintentional excess is harmless.

Materials for Stoning: The General Rule and the Condition of Humiliation
Ruling on stoning materials and the condition of humiliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general rule for permissible stoning materials, explain the condition of istihana, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding precious stones.

Core Idea
Stoning must humiliate—precious materials that honor the target are impermissible.

The stoning of the jamarat is an act of worship meant to degrade the devil. The Hanafi school therefore holds that the thrown object should be something lowly, from the earth's genus. This passage explains the general rule and the major intra-Hanafi debate about whether precious stones like ruby and turquoise are allowed, hinging on the condition of istihana (humiliation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exceptions
Read the passage to find what materials are generally permissible (from the earth) and which are explicitly forbidden (wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, silver). List them.
The permissibility extends to anything of the earth's genus (jins al-ard).
2
Understand the reasons for prohibition
The author gives three reasons: not from earth, not a proper throw (nthār), or exaltation (i'zāz) rather than humiliation. Identify which reason applies to which forbidden material.
Gold and silver are classified as nthār; jewels and pearls as not from earth; wood and amber as exaltation.
3
Trace the dispute on precious stones
The passage presents disagreement: some (like al-Hidaya, al-Zayla'i) allow precious stones because they are from earth; others (the commentators, ash-sharhūn) forbid them based on istihana. Follow the references to al-Inaya, al-Ghaya, etc.
The key point is whether the condition of istihana is additional to being from earth.
4
Identify the relied-upon position
Examine the text's conclusion: 'يفيد ترجيح اعتبار الشرط' – it indicates preference for considering the condition. Thus the muftā bihi is that precious stones are impermissible.
This is a later development; earlier texts like al-Hidaya did not stipulate istihana.
5
Apply the ruling to a new case
Given the condition of istihana, determine the ruling for materials like marble, crushed brick, or diamond dust. Check if they are from the earth and whether they affirm humiliation.
Marble is from earth but may be considered 'precious' – needs scrutiny.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فيجوز الرمي بالحصى لبيان الأكمل وإلا فيجوز الرمي بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض كالحجر والمدر وما يجوز التيمم به ولو كفاً من تراب ، ولا يجوز بالخشب والعنبر واللؤلؤ والجواهر والذهب والفضة، إما لأنها ليست نفي ذلك الاشتراط. وممن ذكر جوازه الفار مناسكه كذا في الفتح. وهذا يفيد ترجيح اعتبار الشرط المذكور، ومقتضى كلام رسي في الشارح تبعاً للغاية عدم اعتباره حيث جزما بجوازه بالأحجار النفيسة بخلاف الخشب ) ذلك يجوز الرمي بهما وأجيب بأن الجواز مشروط بالاستهانة برميه وذلك لا يحصل بهما اهـ. فقد أثبت تخصيص العموم وهو مخالف لنص الزيلعي، وخصص بالفيروزج والياقوت دون غيرهما فليتأمل ويحرر ا هـ . بقي شيء وهو أن الزيلعي استثنى الجواهر وتبعه أنه المؤلف مع صرح بجواز الأحجار النفيسة ولم يذكر الجواهر العيني ولا الشمني . قال نوح أفندي : لأنها من قبيل الأحجار النفيسة بل الأحجار النفيسة مستخرجة منها، وفي حاشية مسكين : تفرقة الزيلعي بين الجواهر والأحجار النفيسة في الحكم ليس إلا محض تحكم ا هـ . لكن ذكر الشيخ إسماعيل في شرحه عن الغاية : والجواهر وهي كبار اللؤلؤ وبه اندفع التحكم لأنها ليست من جنس الأرض . وممن اعترض على العناية بما في الغاية والزيلعي سعدي أفندي في حواشيه عليها وسبقه إليه في التتارخانية فإنه بعد ما ذكر الاعتراض والجواب السابقين وعزاهما إلى السغناقي قال: واعلم أن هذه الرواية مخالفة لما في المحيط أي من الجواز بكل ما كان . مر عن الهداية قوله : (إما الأرض كما . من جنس لأنها ليست من جنس الأرض هذا خاص فيما قبل الذهب والفضة. وقوله وإما لأنها نثار خاص بهما كما هو مذكور في السعدية عن الغاية، وقوله (وإما لأنه إعزاز «الخ يشمل الكل إلا الخشب إن كان مما ليس له قيمة قوله : (كما ورد في الحديث جعله في الهداية أثراً . وقال في الفتح: وقوله «به ورد الأثر» كأنه ما عن سعيد بن جبير قلت لابن عباس : ما بال الجمار ترمى من وقت الخليل عليه السلام ولم تصر هضاباً تسد الأفق ؟ فقال : أما علمت أن من يقبل حجه يرفع حصاه قال : ومن لم يقبل ترك حصاه .
Otherwise, throwing with pebbles is permissible to indicate the most complete; otherwise, throwing is permissible with everything that is of the type of earth, like stone, clod, and what is permissible for tayammum, even a handful of dust. It is not permissible with wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, and silver, either because they are not of the type of earth, or because they are (like) scattered things and not (proper) throwing, or because it is exaltation, not humiliation. Likewise, the restriction to pebbles of khidhf is to indicate the most perfect; for if he throws with a larger stone, it is permissible because the objective is achieved, (but) stones (should be) so that others are not harmed; and if he throws (with a large stone), it is valid but disliked. He did not specify from where to take the pebbles because it is permissible to take them from any place; so let him take them from Muzdalifa or from the highway, but it is disliked (tanzihan) to take them from near the jamrah because it is the pebbles of the one whose hajj was not accepted; for the one whose hajj is accepted, his pebbles are raised, as reported in the hadith. He did not require purity of the stones because it is permissible to throw with a ritually impure stone, except that (it is not) the spot ... In al-Nahr: The absolute wording gives permissibility with ruby and turquoise, and there is disagreement about them. The commentators and others forbade it based on the condition of humiliation (istihana) of the thrown object; some allowed it based on negating that condition. Among those who mentioned its permissibility is al-Far in his ritual manual; thus in al-Fath. This indicates a preference for considering the aforementioned condition. The implication of the words of Rasi in the commentary following al-Ghaya is non-consideration of it, where they definitively permit throwing with precious stones, unlike wood, amber, and pearls (i.e., large ones) because they are not parts of the earth. As for gold and silver, they are scattered and not (proper) throwing. So ends. In al-Shirnilbaliyya, we presented the permissibility of throwing with everything of the type of earth, and among those who explicitly stated it is the author of al-Hidaya, so it includes all precious stones like ruby, chrysolite, emerald, belakhsh, turquoise, crystal, and agate. This is what al-Zayla'i explicitly stated, except that in al-Inaya he said: Objection was raised against the author of al-Hidaya regarding turquoise and ruby, for they are parts of the earth such that tayammum is permissible with them; yet they are permissible for throwing. He answered that permissibility is conditioned by humiliation in throwing it, and that is not achieved with them. So he established a specification of the general, and this contradicts the text of al-Zayla'i. He specified turquoise and ruby but not others, so consider and write down. One thing remains: al-Zayla'i excluded jewels and the author followed him, while the author explicitly permitted precious stones and did not mention jewels; al-Ayni nor al-Shumni mentioned them. Nuh Afandi said: Because they are of the category of precious stones; rather, precious stones are extracted from them. In the marginalia of Miskin, the distinction of al-Zayla'i between jewels and precious stones in ruling is pure arbitrariness. But Shaykh Ismail in his commentary from al-Ghaya said: Jewels are large pearls, and by this the arbitrariness is refuted because they are not of the type of earth. Among those who objected to al-Inaya based on al-Ghaya and al-Zayla'i is Sa'di Efendi in his marginalia on it, preceded by that in al-Tatarjaniyya; after mentioning the objection and the preceding answer, attributing them to al-Saghnaqi, he said: Know that this narration is contrary to what is in al-Muhit, i.e., permissibility with everything of the type of earth. He passed by al-Hidaya's saying: 'Either because they are not of the earth' is specific to what precedes gold and silver. His saying: 'or because they are scattered' is specific to them, as mentioned in al-Sa'diyya from al-Ghaya. His saying: 'or because it is exaltation' includes all except wood if it has no value. His saying: 'as reported in the hadith' – he made it in al-Hidaya as an athar. In al-Fath, his saying: 'with it the athar is reported' seems to be what (is narrated) from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: I said to Ibn Abbas: What is the matter that the jamarat are thrown from the time of al-Khalil (Ibrahim) and they have not become heaps blocking the horizon? He said: Do you not know that the one whose hajj is accepted, his pebbles are raised; and the one whose hajj is not accepted, his pebbles are left.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling about what materials are permissible for stoning in Hajj. The author explains that the ideal is to use small pebbles (حصى الخذف), but it is permissible to throw anything that is from the earth (جنس الأرض) such as stone, dried mud, or even a handful of dust. It is not permissible to use wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, or silver. The reasons are threefold: (1) these items are not from the earth; (2) they are scattered (نثار) and not proper throwing; (3) using them would be an honor (إعزاز) to the target instead of humiliation (إهانة). The stoning is meant to degrade the devil, so the thrown object should be something lowly. Larger stones are valid but disliked because they may harm others. The source of the pebbles is not specified; they can be taken from anywhere, but it is disliked to take them from near the jamrah because there is a tradition that the pebbles of the accepted hajj are raised up. Purity of the stones is not required; even a najis (ritually impure) stone can be used. A major discuession follows regarding precious stones (الياقوت, الفيروزج, etc.). Some scholars, like the author of al-Hidaya, include them as permissible because they are from the earth. However, others (ash-sharhun) forbid them based on the condition of istihana (humiliation) – because such precious stones are not humble. The dispute is detailed: the commentator al-Zayla'i permits precious stones but forbids jewels (الجواهر) like large pearls, because they are not from the earth. The author tends to side with the condition of istihana, but the text shows multiple opinions. Eventually, the passage cites the hadith through Ibn Abbas explaining why pebbles do not accumulate – the pebbles of accepted pilgrims are removed.

Key Terms
إعزاز لا إهانة (i'zaz la ihana): Giving honor, not humiliation. Used as a reason to forbid throwing precious substances because they honor the target instead of degrading it.
الاستهانة (al-istihana): Humiliation; the condition that the thrown object should be humble and lowly.
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of earth; materials that are natural from the earth's crust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, throwing which of the following materials is impermissible due to the condition of istihana?
A) A piece of ordinary limestone
B) A handful of dust
C) A small ruby
D) A clod of dried mud

Key Takeaway
Stoning must be done with something lowly; precious stones are forbidden in the later Hanafi position because they exalt rather than humiliate.

Ruling on Permissible Materials for Ramy and Dispute on Precious Stones
Ruling on permissible substances for ramy with intra-Hanafi dispute on precious stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible substances for ramy, distinguish between the basic rule and the intra-Hanafi dispute on precious stones, and evaluate the role of the condition of humiliation (ihanah) in tarjih.

Core Idea
Ramy is valid only with earth-like substances; using precious stones is disputed because they may honor rather than humiliate.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author presents the ruling on what substances may be used for throwing pebbles (ramy) during Hajj. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq lays down the general rule: only materials from the genus of the earth (jins al-ard) are permissible. It then lists prohibited materials and gives rationales. The commentary expands into a significant intra-Hanafi dispute over precious stones like ruby (yakut) and turquoise (firuzaj), revolving around whether the condition of humiliation (ihanah) is required. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly applying the mufta bihi position in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its conditions
Read the matn: ramy is permissible with anything from jins al-ard (stone, clod, sand, etc.). Prohibited are wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, silver. Three rationales are given. Recognize that the default is permissibility for earth-like substances.
The matn's phrase 'جنس الأرض' is key.
2
Locate the point of ikhtilaf
Find where the commentary introduces the dispute: after stating the apparent unrestrictedness (إطلاق) gives permissibility for yakut and firuzaj. Note that the dispute is about precious stones, not the basic prohibited list.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi, not between schools.
3
State the arguments of the permissibility group
Al-Hidayah and al-Zaylai allow precious stones because they are from jins al-ard, as established by the permissibility of tayammum with them. They do not require ihanah as a condition.
Their dalil is qiyas on tayammum and jins al-ard.
4
State the arguments of the prohibition group
Commentators like al-Inayah require the condition of humiliation (ihanah). They argue that using valuable items honors the ritual (i'zaz) rather than humiliates the devil (ihanah). The matn's own phrase 'إعزاز لا إهانة' supports this.
This group restricts the general permission by adding a condition.
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
Al-Bahr al-Raiq indicates that Fath al-Qadir prefers the condition of ihanah. Later Hanafi scholars like the author of al-Inayah and al-Sharnablali adopt this view. The mufta bihi is that precious stones are not valid for ramy.
The tarjih is based on the spirit of the act and later authoritative fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالحصى لبيان الأكمل وإلا فيجوز الرمي بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض كالحجر والمدر وما يجوز التيمم به ولو كفاً من تراب ، ولا يجوز بالخشب والعنبر واللؤلؤ والجواهر والذهب والفضة، إما لأنها ليست من جنس الأرض أو لأنها نثار وليست برمي أو لأنه إعزاز لا إهانة، وكذا التقييد بحصى الخذف لبيان الأكمل فإنه لو رماها بأكبر منه جاز لحصول المقصود الحجارة كيلا يتأذى به غيره ولو رمي صح وكره. (الخ) قال . في النهر : ظاهر الإطلاق يعطي جوازه بالياقوت والفيروزج وفيهما خلاف، ومنعه الشارحون وغيرهم بناء على اشتراط الاستهانة بالمرمى، وأجازه بعضهم بناء على نفي ذلك الاشتراط. وممن ذكر جوازه الفار مناسكه كذا في الفتح. وهذا يفيد ترجيح اعتبار الشرط المذكور، ومقتضى كلام رسي [؟] في الشارح تبعاً للغاية عدم اعتباره حيث جزما بجوازه بالأحجار النفيسة بخلاف الخشب والعنبر واللؤلؤ يعني كباره لأنها ليست من أجزاء الأرض، وأما الذهب والفضة فنثار وليست برمي ا هـ. وفي الشرنبلالية قدمنا جواز الرمي بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض، وممن صرح به صاحب الهداية فشمل كل الأحجار النفيسة كالياقوت والزبرجد والزمرد والبلخش الفيروزج والبلور والعقيق. وبهذا صرح الزيلعي إلا أنه قال في العناية : اعترض على صاحب الهداية بالفيروزج والياقوت فإنهما من أجزاء الأرض حتى جاز التيمم بهما، ومع ) ذلك يجوز الرمي بهما وأجيب بأن الجواز مشروط بالاستهانة برميه وذلك لا يحصل بهما اهـ. فقد أثبت تخصيص العموم وهو مخالف لنص الزيلعي، وخصص بالفيروزج والياقوت دون غيرهما فليتأمل ويحرر ا هـ . بقي شيء وهو أن الزيلعي استثنى الجواهر وتبعه أنه المؤلف مع صرح بجواز الأحجار النفيسة ولم يذكر الجواهر العيني ولا الشمني . قال نوح أفندي : لأنها من قبيل الأحجار النفيسة بل الأحجار النفيسة مستخرجة منها، وفي حاشية مسكين : تفرقة الزيلعي بين الجواهر والأحجار النفيسة في الحكم ليس إلا محض تحكم ا هـ . لكن ذكر الشيخ إسماعيل في شرحه عن الغاية : والجواهر وهي كبار اللؤلؤ وبه اندفع التحكم لأنها ليست من جنس الأرض . وممن اعترض على العناية بما في الغاية والزيلعي سعدي أفندي في حواشيه عليها وسبقه إليه في التتارخانية فإنه بعد ما ذكر الاعتراض والجواب السابقين وعزاهما إلى السغناقي قال: واعلم أن هذه الرواية مخالفة لما في المحيط أي من الجواز بكل ما كان . مر عن الهداية قوله : (إما الأرض كما . من جنس لأنها ليست من جنس الأرض هذا خاص فيما قبل الذهب والفضة. وقوله وإما لأنها نثار خاص بهما كما هو مذكور في السعدية عن الغاية، وقوله (وإما لأنه إعزاز «الخ يشمل الكل إلا الخشب إن كان مما ليس له قيمة
With pebbles to indicate the most complete, otherwise it is permissible to throw with everything that is of the genus of the earth, like stone and clod and what is permissible to perform tayammum with, even a handful of dust. And it is not permissible with wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, and silver, either because they are not of the genus of the earth, or because they are scattered and not throwing, or because it is honoring not humiliating. Similarly, the restriction to pebbles of the size used for throwing (khadhf) is to indicate the most complete; if he throws with something larger than that, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but to prevent others from being harmed, and if he throws (with large stones) it is valid but disliked. (End of matn) He said in al-Nahr: The apparent unrestrictedness gives its permissibility with ruby and turquoise, and there is a dispute concerning them. The commentators and others prevented it based on the condition of humiliation in the thrown object, and some permitted it based on negating that condition. Among those who mentioned its permissibility is al-Far in his Manasik, as in al-Fath. This indicates a preference for considering the mentioned condition. The implication of the words of Ramli [؟] in the sharh, following al-Ghayah, is that it is not considered, as they definitively said it is permissible with precious stones, unlike wood, amber, and pearls, meaning large ones, because they are not of the parts of the earth. As for gold and silver, they are scattered and not throwing. In al-Sharnablaliyya, we presented the permissibility of throwing with everything that is of the genus of the earth, and among those who stated it is the author of al-Hidayah, so it includes all precious stones like ruby, chrysolite, emerald, balakhsh, turquoise, crystal, and agate. And al-Zaylai stated this except that he said in al- Inayah: An objection was raised against the author of al-Hidayah regarding turquoise and ruby, for they are parts of the earth such that tayammum with them is permissible, and yet throwing with them is permissible. The answer was that permissibility is conditioned on humiliation in throwing it, and that is not achieved with them. So he established a specification of the general and it contradicts the text of al-Zaylai, and he specified with turquoise and ruby only, not others, so it should be considered and determined. There remains an issue: al-Zaylai excluded jewels and followed that the author (of the matn) with his explicit permissibility of precious stones did not mention jewels, and al-Ayni and al-Shumnuni did not mention them. Nuh Afandi said: Because they are of the category of precious stones, rather precious stones are extracted from them. In the marginalia of Miskin: The distinction of al-Zaylai between jewels and precious stones in the ruling is nothing but pure arbitrariness. But Shaykh Ismail mentioned in his sharh from al-Ghayah: Jewels are large pearls, and thus the arbitrariness is repelled because they are not of the genus of the earth. Among those who objected to al-Inayah based on what is in al-Ghayah and al-Zaylai is Sa'di Afandi in his marginalia upon it, and preceded him in al-Tatarkhaniyya, for after mentioning the objection and the previous answer and attributing them to al-Sighnaqi, he said: Know that this narration contradicts what is in al-Muhit, i.e., the permissibility with everything that is of the genus of the earth. From al-Hidayah: His statement (either because they are not of the genus of the earth) is specific regarding what was before gold and silver. His statement (or because they are scattered) is specific to those two (gold and silver) as is mentioned in al-Sa'diyya from al-Ghayah, and his statement (or because it is honoring ...) includes everything except wood if it is something that has no value.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq with extensive commentary (sharh) from al-Bahr al-Raiq. The matn states that the complete (akmal) way is to throw with pebbles of a specific size (khadhf), but it is permissible to throw with any earth-like substance (jins al-ard), including stone, clod, or anything with which tayammum is valid, such as a handful of dust. Throwing with wood, amber, pearls, jewels, gold, or silver is not permissible. Three rationales are given: these items are not from the genus of the earth; they are scattered (nithar) rather than proper throwing; or using them constitutes honoring (i'zaz) the ritual rather than humiliating (ihanah) it, which is the intended spirit of ramy. Using larger stones is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it may harm others. The commentary then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about precious stones like ruby (yakut) and turquoise (firuzaj). Some scholars, including the author of al-Hidayah and al-Zaylai, allow them because they are also from the genus of the earth. Others, including the commentators and the author of al-Inayah, require the condition of humiliation (ihanah) and thus prohibit them. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq notes that the statement from Fath al-Qadir indicates a preference for the condition of humiliation. The discussion extends to jewels (jawahir), with some Hanafis distinguishing them from precious stones, while others reject this distinction as arbitrary. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that only earth-like substances are valid; precious stones are not valid because the condition of humiliation is not fulfilled, though some later Hanafis allowed them. The commentary cites various Hanafi authorities including al-Sharnablali, al-Zaylai, al-Ayni, and others.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of the earth, i.e., materials that are composed of earth or mineral substances like stone, clod, sand.
إعزاز (i'zaz): Honoring or ennobling, the opposite of humiliation; used to explain why certain valuable materials are not suitable for ramy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) on throwing with a ruby (yakut) for ramy?
A) Valid because it is a stone and thus from jins al-ard.
B) Invalid because it is not from jins al-ard.
C) Invalid because it does not fulfill the condition of humiliation (ihanah).
D) Valid because it is similar to tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits ramy only with earth-like substances; using precious stones is generally invalid due to the requirement of humiliation, though earlier scholars allowed them.

Ruling on Where to Take Pebbles and Purity Thereof
Ruling on location for collecting pebbles, hadith of accepted pebbles, and purity issue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the location for collecting pebbles for ramy, identify the disliked place and its rationale, and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Pebbles may be taken from anywhere; Muzdalifah is recommended, but near the jamrah is disliked due to rejected hajj.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on where a pilgrim should collect the pebbles for stoning the jamarat. While the general principle is permissibility, the school recommends certain locations and discourages others based on a prophetic tradition. The lesson also addresses the often-asked question of whether the pebbles must be ritually pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling on location
Read the matn: 'ولم يبين وذ منه الحصا لأنه يجوز أخذه من أي موضع شاء'. The author states that the place is not specified; it is permissible to take pebbles from any place. This is the baseline.
The default is mubah (permissible), not restricted.
2
Note the recommended and disliked places
The text then says: 'فليأخذها من مزدلفة أو من قارعة الطريق، ويكره من عند الجمرة تنزيهاً'. Identify that Muzdalifah and the roadside are recommended (mustahabb), while near the jamrah is disliked (makruh tanzihan).
Dislike is due to association with rejected hajj.
3
Analyze the evidence for the dislike
The commentary provides a hadith (or athar) that pebbles of an accepted hajj are raised; those left behind are from rejected hajj. This implies that pebbles near the jamrah may be from rejected hajj, hence disliked.
The evidence is zanni in transmission and indication.
4
Understand the ruling on purity of pebbles
The matn states 'ولم يشترط طهارة الحجارة لأنه يجوز الرمي بالحجر النجس'. The Hanafi school does not require the pebbles to be pure; even najis stones are valid for ramy, though washing is preferred.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
5
Distinguish the Hanafi position from a misconception
The commentary clarifies that taking from Muzdalifah is not obligatory (wajib) but recommended. The phrase 'ليس مذهبنا' refers to the view that pebbles must be taken exclusively from Muzdalifah.
Al-Hidayah affirms permissibility from any place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يبين وذ منه الحصا لأنه يجوز أخذه من أي موضع شاء فليأخذها من مزدلفة أو من قارعة الطريق، ويكره من عند الجمرة تنزيهاً لأنه حصى من لم يقبل حجه فإنه من قبل حجه رفع حصاه كما ورد في الحديث. ولم يشترط طهارة الحجارة لأنه يجوز الرمي بالحجر النجس غير أنه لا الموضع بالكبار من يرمي المأخوذ الخ) قال . قوله : (كما ورد في الحديث) جعله في الهداية أثراً . وقال في الفتح: وقوله «به ورد الأثر» كأنه ما عن سعيد بن جبير قلت لابن عباس : ما بال الجمار ترمى من وقت الخليل عليه السلام ولم تصر هضاباً تسد الأفق ؟ فقال : أما علمت أن من يقبل حجه يرفع حصاه قال : ومن لم يقبل ترك حصاه . قال مجاهد : لما سمعت هذا من ابن عباس جعلت على حصياتي علامة ثم توسطت الجمرة فرميت من كل جانب ثم طلبت فلم أجد بتلك العلامة شيئاً ) لكن في حاشيه المدني عن شرح النقاية لمنلا علي القاري أنه رواه الدارقطني والحاكم وصححه عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال قلت: يا رسول الله هذه الجمار التي نرمي بها كل عام فنحسب أنها تنقص فقال : إنه ما يقبل منها رفع ولولا ذلك لرأيتها أمثال الجبال ! هـ. واستشكله ابن كمال باشا بأن حج المشركين غير مقبول. وأجيب بأن الكفار قد تقبل عباداتهم فيجازون عليها في الدنيا أقول : المراد أعمالهم التي هي عبادات صورة لا حقيقة لأن مثل الحج لا يكون عبادة إلا بالنية والكافر ليس من أهلها كما صرحوا به تأمل. هذا وفي منى خمس آيات هذه إحداها وقد نظمها بعضهم فقال : وآي منى خمس فمنها اتساعها لحجاج بيت الله لـو جـاوزوا الحدا ومنع حداة خطف لحم بأرضها وقلة وجدان البعوض بها عدا وكون ذباب لا يعاقب طعمها ورفع حصى المقبول دون الذي ردا قوله: (وليس) مذهبنا قال في الشرنبلالية يعارضه قول الجوهرة: ويستحب أن يأخذ حصى لجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق ا هـ . ولذا قال في الهداية : يأخذ الحصى من أي موضع شاء ا هـ. فالنفي ليس إلا على التعيين أي لا يتعين الأخذ من المزدلفة لنا مذهباً، وما قاله في الهداية يقتضي خلاف ما قيل إنه يلتقطها من الجبل الذي على الطريق في المزدلفة، وما قيل يأخذ من المزدلفة سبعاً فأفاد أنه لا سنة ذلك في يوجب خلافها الإساءة
And he did not specify where to take the pebbles because it is permissible to take them from any place he wishes. So let him take them from Muzdalifah or from the side of the road. And it is disliked (tanzihan) from near the jamrah because they are pebbles of one whose hajj was not accepted, for indeed one whose hajj is accepted, his pebbles are raised, as came in the hadith. And he did not require purity of the stones because it is permissible to throw with a najis stone, except that ... (commentary) His statement: (as came in the hadith) al-Hidayah made it an athar. And in al-Fath: His statement 'with it came the athar' is as if it is from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: I said to Ibn Abbas: Why are the jamarat thrown from the time of al-Khalil (peace be upon him) and they do not become hills blocking the horizon? He said: Do you not know that one whose hajj is accepted, his pebbles are raised? He said: And one whose hajj is not accepted, his pebbles are left. Mujahid said: When I heard this from Ibn Abbas, I placed a mark on my pebbles, then I encircled the jamrah and threw from every side, then I sought and did not find anything with that mark. But in the marginalia of al-Madani from Sharh al-Niqayah of Mulla Ali al-Qari that al-Daraqutni and al-Hakim reported and authenticated it from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, these jamarat which we throw every year and we think they decrease? He said: Indeed, what is accepted from them is raised, and were it not for that, you would see them like mountains! This is problematic for Ibn Kamal Basha because the hajj of polytheists is not accepted. And it was answered that disbelievers may have their acts of worship accepted and are rewarded for them in this world. I say: What is meant is their deeds that are forms of worship not reality, because hajj is only a worship with intention, and the disbeliever is not of its people as they stated. Consider. This, and in Mina there are five signs; this is one of them. Someone organized them in poetry: And the signs of Mina are five: its spaciousness for the pilgrims of the House of Allah if they exceed the limit, and preventing the collectors of sacrificial flesh from snatching meat in its land, and the scarcity of finding mosquitoes there besides, and that flies are not harmed by its meat, and the raising of the pebbles of the accepted without those rejected. His statement: (it is not) our school. He said in al-Sharnablaliyya: It is contradicted by the statement of al-Jawhara: It is recommended to take pebbles for the jamarat from Muzdalifah or from the road. Therefore, al-Hidayah said: He takes pebbles from any place he wishes. So the negation is only of specification, meaning that taking from Muzdalifah is not obligatory in our school. And what al-Hidayah said implies contrary to what is said that he picks them from the mountain on the road in Muzdalifah, and what is said that he takes from Muzdalifah seven, so it indicates that there is no sunnah in that, and opposing it incurs blameworthy action.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage continues the matn and commentary on the chapter of ihram. The matn states that the place from which pebbles are taken is not specified; they may be taken from anywhere, but it is recommended to take them from Muzdalifah or the roadside. Taking them from near the jamrah is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because those pebbles belong to people whose hajj was not accepted, as indicated by a hadith that pebbles of accepted hajj are raised up. The matn also says that purity of the pebbles is not required; one may throw with a najis stone, though it is preferred to wash them. The commentary then provides the narrative of the hadith from Ibn Abbas and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about the pebbles being raised, along with a discussion of a possible problem regarding polytheists' hajj, which is resolved by noting that their worship may be accepted in this world in form. The commentary also mentions that there are five miraculous signs (ayat) of Mina, one of which is this raising of accepted pebbles. Finally, the commentary clarifies that the statement 'it is not our school' refers to the notion that pebbles must be taken only from Muzdalifah; rather, it is permissible from anywhere, and taking from Muzdalifah is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A location between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night and collect pebbles.
أثر (athar): A saying or action of a Sahabi (companion), as opposed to a hadith marfu' (from the Prophet).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From where is it disliked (makruh tanzihan) to take pebbles for ramy according to the Hanafi school?
A) From Muzdalifah
B) From the side of the road
C) From near the jamrah
D) From any place

Key Takeaway
Pebbles for ramy may be taken from any clean place; Muzdalifah is recommended, but near the jamrah is disliked due to the hadith of raised pebbles; purity is not required.

Timings of Ramy al-Jamar and the Ruling on Delay
Explanation of the four times for ramy and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on delay causing dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of ramy al-jamar and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the obligation of dam for delay.

Core Idea
Delaying ramy beyond dawn of the next day triggers a dam according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

Ramy al-jamar is a wajib ritual of Hajj performed on specific days. While the general time is from dawn of the 10th to dawn of the 11th, scholars differ on what happens if one delays. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the four categories of time and the ensuing debate between the founding Imams of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four times for ramy
The imam explains that ramy has four categories: time of permissibility (jawaz), recommendation (istihbab), neutrality (ibahah), and dislike (karahah). The permissible time starts at dawn of the 10th and ends at dawn of the 11th.
These categories reflect different levels of desirability within the valid timeframe.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling on delay
If one delays ramy until after dawn of the 11th, a dam becomes wajib according to Abu Hanifa. This is because the delay is a violation of the prescribed time, akin to other Hajj violations.
The term 'dam' refers to a sacrificial animal.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree; they hold that no dam is required for delaying past dawn of the 11th. The ramy is still valid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the qada' issue
According to Fath al-Qadir, if ramy is delayed until after sunset of the same day, it becomes qada' (make-up) according to Abu Hanifa, but no penalty other than blame (isaa'ah) if there is no excuse.
This shows a nuance: not all delays require a dam.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a pilgrim who delays without excuse must offer a dam according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn consider it valid without extra penalty. The mufta bihi leans toward Abu Hanifa.
A mufti should be aware of both views but follow the relied-upon position.

And he did not specify its time, and it has four times: the time of permissibility, the time of recommendation, the time of permissibility (mubah), and the time of dislike. The first: its beginning is from dawn of the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) and its end is when dawn of the second day rises, such that if he delays until dawn of the second day, a dam becomes obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Commentary
This passage covers the timing of ramy al-jamar on the Day of Nahr and the following days. The matn states that there are four categories of time for ramy: permissible (ja'iz), recommended (mustahabb), mubah (neutral), and disliked (makruh). The permissible time begins at dawn of the 10th and ends at dawn of the next day (11th). If one delays ramy until after dawn of the 11th, a dam (sacrificial animal) is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) disagree and hold that no dam is required. The commentary then notes that according to Fath al-Qadir, if ramy is delayed until after sunset, it becomes qada' (make-up) according to Abu Hanifa, but no penalty other than blame (isaa'ah) if there is no excuse. The commentary also references a disagreement among Hanafi sources: some (like al-Mabsut) extend the permissible time until sunset of the same day, while others (like al-Hidayah) say from dawn to sunset. The author reconciles these by noting that in zahir al-madhhab (the apparent school position), the time is until sunset, but throwing at night is still valid without penalty.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (e.g., a sheep) required as compensation for certain violations or delays in Hajj rituals.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory act after its time has passed.

Preparing Pebbles for Ramy: Washing and Source
Commentary on washing and sourcing pebbles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing pebbles for ramy and explain the ikhtilaf regarding the obligation of taking them from Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Washing pebbles is recommended, not required; pebbles may be taken from anywhere, though Muzdalifah is preferred.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the preferred practices for preparing the pebbles used in the stoning ritual (ramy) during Hajj. He addresses two related issues: washing the pebbles, and the dispute over whether they must be taken from Muzdalifah. We will explore the proofs and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended status
The phrase 'al-afdal ghasluha' indicates that washing is best (afdal), placing it in the category of mustahab (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
Afdal in fiqh usually implies strong recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the proof for washing
The author does not cite a specific hadith here, but the general practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the principle of cleanliness support this recommendation.
The hadith about pebbles being raised (cited later) indirectly supports the merit of the act.
3
Identify the dispute about taking pebbles from Muzdalifah
Some sources (e.g., al-Hasiri, al-Kirmani) and some non-Hanafis specify taking pebbles from Muzdalifah or the mountain on the road. The author states that this is not the Hanafi madhhab.
The dispute is whether the source is specified or general.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Al-Hidayah asserts that the pilgrim may take pebbles from wherever he wishes. The negation 'not our madhhab' refers only to specification (ta'yin), not to recommendation.
The Hanafi position allows flexibility, while still preferring Muzdalifah based on practice.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that washing is recommended, and pebbles may be taken from any location, though it is better to take from Muzdalifah. There is no sin in opposing the recommended act.
This ruling is consistent with the principle that the stoning itself is the obligation, not the ancillary acts.

So it indicates that there is no sunnah in that such that opposing it would cause offense.

Commentary
This passage addresses the preferred method of obtaining and preparing pebbles for the stoning ritual (ramy). The author begins by stating that washing the pebbles is best (فضل) and then presents various opinions from different works. Al-Hasiri's Manasik mentions a practice of carrying 70 pebbles from a mountain on the road, while al-Kirmani's Manasik mentions throwing from Muzdalifah with seven pebbles. The author clarifies that the Hanafi madhhab is not that of the group who say seventy. Fath al-Qadir reports that it is disliked to break one stone into seventy small ones, a practice common among many people. The passage then shifts to the time of ramy, listing four times: permissibility, recommendation, permission, and dislike. Abu Hanifa's view that delaying until the second day's dawn obligates a dam is noted, with a disagreement from the Sahibayn. A hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is cited to show that accepted pebbles are raised up, proving their acceptance. The author then addresses an objection regarding disbelievers' Hajj not being accepted, explaining that their actions are worship only in form, not reality. A poem about the verses of Mina is included. Finally, the commentary returns to the issue of taking pebbles from Muzdalifah, concluding that the negation 'not our madhhab' refers only to specifying Muzdalifah as the unique source, while in reality taking from any place is permissible per al-Hidayah, and opposing the recommended but non-obligatory practice does not cause sin.

Key Terms
غسلها (ghasluha): Washing the pebbles before throwing them; considered a recommended act (mustahab) in this context.
حصى (hasa): Pebbles used for stoning the Jamarat; typically seven in number for each Jamrah.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): The place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night and collect pebbles for stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Washing pebbles is a recommended sunnah, and pebbles may be taken from any place; the obligation is only on the act of stoning itself.

Times for Ramy and the Consequence of Delay: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explanation of four ramy times and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the four time classifications for ramy on the Day of Nahr and apply Abu Hanifa's view on the requirement of a dam for delay until dawn of the second day.

Core Idea
Delaying ramy beyond the first day may incur a dam (penalty) according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn disagree.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute about the times when ramy (stoning the Jamarat) is valid and the consequences of delay. You will learn the four time categories from dawn of the Day of Nahr to the following day, and delve into the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether a dam (penalty) is required if the pilgrim delays ramy until dawn of the second day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that ramy is a wajib act in Hajj. Then note how the time discussion affects its validity and penalty.
Ramy itself is wajib; missing it requires a dam, but timing affects whether the dam applies.
2
Understand the time classification
The passage divides the time for ramy into four periods: from dawn to sunrise (valid), sunrise to midday (recommended), midday to sunset (valid), and before sunrise or after sunset (disliked but valid).
According to al-Muhit and others, the first and third are times of jawaz; the second is mustahabb; the fourth is makruh.
3
Locate the dispute
The disagreement centres on what happens if ramy is delayed until dawn of the second day. Abu Hanifa says a dam becomes necessary; the Sahibayn say no dam is required.
The text states that the majority side with Abu Hanifa.
4
Examine the evidence
Abu Hanifa's view is based on the idea that the time for performance ends at sunset, and delay beyond that triggers qada (make-up) and thus a dam. The Sahibayn consider the time of permissibility extends till dawn of the second day, so no penalty.
The text cites al-Fath for Abu Hanifa's view and al-Mabsut for the Sahibayn's position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a pilgrim who delays ramy till after dawn of the second day must offer a dam according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa), whereas according to the Sahibayn, no dam is needed.
The majority view is with Abu Hanifa, making it the mufta bihi.

He said: (And its end is when dawn rises, etc.) In it is that the time of permissibility has no end, because by it is meant validity not permissibility, so it is best not to mention the end as in the phrase of al-Mabsut mentioned in al-Fath. Then it appeared to me the answer that he intended to explain the time of permissibility for performance as expressed in Sharh al-Lubab, but in al-Fath: And the description of making up (qada) is established for ramy from sunset in the view of Abu Hanifa, except that there is nothing in it except the establishment of offense if there was no excuse. Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage explains the times for ramy (stoning) on the Day of Nahr and the following day. The commentator discusses a statement about the time ending at dawn of the second day, noting that according to some, the time of permissibility has no end because it concerns validity, not permissibility. However, he offers an interpretation that it refers to the performance time. Then he notes that in al-Fath, Abu Hanifa considers that if one delays beyond sunset, it becomes qada (make-up), and there is nothing else except offense if done without excuse. The commentator then cites al-Hidayah and other major works stating that the time is from dawn to sunset. The passage ends with a classification of four times: the first (permissible) from dawn to sunrise, the second (recommended) from sunrise to midday, the third (permissible) from midday to sunset, and the fourth (disliked) before sunrise and after sunset. It also mentions that in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, the permissible time is treated separately, resulting in three divisions, while the majority adhere to the first classification.

Key Terms
وقت الجواز (waqt al-jawaz): The time during which an act is valid and permissible; for ramy, this is from dawn to dawn of the next day according to some, or from dawn to sunset according to others.
دم (dam): A penalty offering (sacrifice) required for serious omissions or delays in Hajj rites, such as delaying ramy beyond its time.
رمي (ramy): The act of stoning the Jamarat, specifically Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr and the three Jamarat on the following days.

C) He must perform the ramy and offer a dam
D) He must only perform the ramy, no penalty

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that delaying ramy until dawn of the second day requires a dam (penalty), following Abu Hanifa's view.

Takbir with Each Pebble and Cutting Talbiyah at Jamrat al-Aqabah
Rules for sunnah acts during ramy: takbir and cutting talbiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) actions during ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah and apply the ruling on cutting talbiyah to different types of pilgrims.

Core Idea
Takbir with each pebble is sunnah, not wajib; cut talbiyah at the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah for all Hajj pilgrims.

The stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib act of Hajj, performed on the Day of Nahr with seven pebbles. While the stoning itself is obligatory, the accompanying actions—such as saying takbir with each pebble and the timing of cutting the talbiyah—follow the Prophet's sunnah. This lesson clarifies these sunnah acts, their proofs, and how they apply to different types of pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm level for saying takbir with each pebble. The text states it is 'best' (أفضل), indicating a sunnah muakkadah, not a wajib. If omitted, the ramy is still valid.
The default assumption might be that verbal utterances during worship are wajib, but here it is explicitly sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil for cutting talbiyah
The hadith in the two Sahihs: 'The Prophet continued to say talbiyah until he threw Jamrat al-Aqabah.' This indicates the moment to cut.
The dalil is sunnah ahad; its thubut is qati but dalala is zanni for the exact ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'until he threw' shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stopped talbiyah at the first pebble. This action implies it is the sunnah to cut there.
The command 'اقطع التلبية بأولها' is derived from this action.
4
Apply to different pilgrims
The ruling applies equally to mufrid, mutamatti', and qarin. Exceptions: mu'tamir cuts at the Black Stone; one who misses Hajj cuts at tawaf of Umrah; muhsar cuts at slaughter; qarin missing Hajj cuts at second tawaf.
The text emphasizes that the restriction to the one in ihram for Hajj is key.
5
Note the wisdom for not standing after Jamrat al-Aqabah
Unlike the other Jamarat, the sunnah is not to stand after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah due to its location on the path causing congestion, as per al-Zahiriyyah.
This practical consideration demonstrates how fiqh accounts for hardship.

Source Text

قوله : (وكبر بكل حصاة أي مع كل حصاة من السبعة بيان للأفضل فلو لم يذكر الله أصلاً أو هلل أو سبح أجزأه ، ولم يذكر الدعاء آخره لأن السنة أن لا يقف عندها كما سيشير إليه في رمي الجمار الثلاث وضابطه أن كل جمرة بعدها جمرة فإنه يقف بعدها للدعاء لأنه في أثناء العبادة، وكل جمرة ليس بعدها جمرة ترمى في يومه لا يقف عندها لأنه خرج من العبادة. كذا في الظهيرية وهو مشكل فإن الدعاء بعد الخروج من العبادة مستحب كما في الصلاة والصوم إذا خرج منهما فالأولى الاستدلال بفعله عليه السلام كذلك وإن لم تظهر له حكمة، وقد يقال هي كون الوقوف يقع في جمرة العقبة في الطريق فيوجب قطع سلوكها على الناس وشدة ازدحام الواقفين والمارين ويفضي ذلك إلى ضرر عظيم بخلافه في باقي الجمرات فإنه لا يقع في نفس الطريق بل بمعزل عنه قوله : واقطع التلبية بأولها) أي مع أول حصاة ترميها لحديث الصحيحين: لم يزل عليه السلام يلبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة. ولا فرق بين المفرد والمتمتع والقارن وقيد بالمحرم بالحج لأن المعتمر يقطع التلبية إذا استلم الحجر لأن الطواف ركن في العمرة فيقطع التلبية قبل الشروع فيها، وقيد بكونه مدركاً للحج بإدراك الوقوف بعرفة لأن فائت الحج إذا تحلل بالعمرة يقطع التلبية حين يأخذ في الطواف لأن العمرة واجبة عليه فصار كالمعتمر والمحصر يقطعها إذا ذبح هديه لأن الذبح للتحلل، والقارن إذا كان فائت الحج يقطع حين يأخذ في الطواف الثاني لأنه يتحلل بعده. وأشار
وعليه يحمل ما قدمناه عن الفتح تأمل قوله : (والثاني من طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال) قال الرملي : أي المستحب وقد وافق على الاستحباب العيني، وذكره في مجمع الرواية عن المحيط أيضاً بصيغة المسنون ووافقه في النهر قوله : (والرابع) قبل طلوع الشمس الخ) قيده في الفتح بعد أحاديث ساقها بعدم العذر قال : حتى لا يكون رمي الضعفة قبل الشمس ورمي الرعاة ليلاً يلزمهم الإساءة وكيف بذلك بعد الترخص قول المصنف : وكبر) بكل حصاة كذا روى ابن مسعود وابن جابر وأم سليمان، وظاهر المرويات من ذلك الاقتصار على «الله أكبر) غير أنه روى عن الحسن بن زياد أنه يقول الله أكبر رغماً للشيطان وخربه». وقيل يقول أيضاً اللهم اجعل حجي مبروراً وسعي مشكوراً وذنبي مغفوراً. كذا في الفتح قوله : ( فالأولى الاستدلال بفعله عليه الخ قال في الفتح : على هذا تظافرت الروايات عنه عليه السلام ولم يظهر حكمة تخصيص الوقوف والدعاء بغيرها من الجمرتين، فإن تخايل أنه في اليوم الأول لكثرة ما عليه من الشغل كالذبح والحلق والإفاضة إلى مكة فهو منعدم فيما بعده من الأيام قوله : ( وقيد بالمحرم بالحج) نسب إليه هذا التقييد وإن لم يكن مصرحاً به، وكذا ما بعده
He said: (And say takbir with each pebble) i.e. with each of the seven pebbles, a statement of the best. For if he did not mention Allah at all, or said "La ilaha illallah" or glorified, it is sufficient. And he did not mention the supplication at the end because the sunnah is not to stand by it, as he will indicate in the stoning of the three Jamarat. The principle: every Jamrah after which there is another Jamrah, he stands after it for supplication because he is in the middle of the worship; and every Jamrah after which there is no Jamrah to be stoned on that day, he does not stand by it because he has exited the worship. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah, but it is problematic, for supplication after exiting worship is recommended, as in prayer and fasting when one exits from them. So it is better to deduce from his action (peace be upon him) like that, even if no wisdom appears. And it is said: it is because standing at Jamrat al-Aqabah occurs in the path, causing interruption of people's movement and severe crowding, leading to great harm, unlike the other Jamarat which are not in the path but away from it. He said: (And cut the talbiyah at its first) i.e. with the first pebble you throw, due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: The Prophet (peace be upon him) continued to say the talbiyah until he threw Jamrat al-Aqabah. There is no distinction between the mufrid (sole Hajj), the mutamatti', and the qarin. It is restricted to the one in ihram for Hajj, because the mutamir cuts the talbiyah when he touches the Black Stone, because tawaf is an integral of Umrah, so he cuts the talbiyah before beginning it. And it is restricted to one who has caught the Hajj by catching the standing at Arafah, because if one misses Hajj and performs tahlul via Umrah, he cuts the talbiyah when he begins tawaf, because Umrah becomes obligatory upon him, so he becomes like a mutamir. And the muhsar (blocked) cuts it when he slaughters his sacrificial animal, because slaughter is for tahlul. And the qarin, if he misses the Hajj, cuts when he begins the second tawaf because he becomes tahlul after it. And he indicated: And upon that is carried what we presented from al-Fath. Ponder. He said: (And the second from sunrise to midday) al-Ramli said: i.e., the recommended. And al-Ayni agreed on recommendation, and he mentioned it in Majma' al-Riwayah from al-Muhit also in the form of "masnun" (established as sunnah), and al-Nahr agreed with him. He said: (And the fourth) before sunrise, etc. He restricted it in al-Fath, after citing hadiths, to one without excuse, saying: So that the throwing of the weak before sunrise and the shepherds at night would incur offense, and how can that be after concession? The author's statement: (And say takbir with each pebble) thus narrated by Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Jabir, and Umm Sulayman. The apparent from the transmitted reports is restriction to "Allahu Akbar", but it is narrated from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that he says: Allahu Akbar, to the frustration of the devil and his ruin. And it is said he also says: O Allah, make my Hajj accepted, my Sa'i appreciated, and my sin forgiven. Thus in al-Fath. He said: (So it is better to deduce from his action, etc.) He said in al-Fath: On this, the narrations from him (peace be upon him) are frequent, and no wisdom has appeared for specifying standing and supplication for others of the two Jamarat. For if it were imagined that on the first day due to much occupation like slaughter, shaving, and ifada to Mecca, that is absent in the days after. He said: (And restricted to the one in ihram for Hajj) this restriction is attributed to him, even if not explicitly stated, and so forth.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah actions during the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah. It begins with the ruling on saying takbir: it is recommended (best) to say 'Allahu Akbar' with each of the seven pebbles. If one fails to do so, the ramy is still valid. The author then addresses whether to stand for supplication after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah. Unlike the other Jamarat, the sunnah is not to stand because it is the last stoning of the day; the pilgrim exits the worship. However, some scholars find this problematic since supplication after worship is generally recommended. A practical wisdom is suggested: Jamrat al-Aqabah is in the main path, causing congestion, so to avoid hardship, the Prophet did not stand there. The passage then explains the cutting of talbiyah: it should be cut with the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah, based on the hadith that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he threw it. This ruling applies to all types of Hajj (mufrid, mutamatti', qarin). Exceptions are mentioned for the mu'tamir (who cuts talbiyah upon touching the Black Stone), the one who missed Hajj and performs tahlul with Umrah (cuts talbiyah when beginning tawaf), the muhsar (cuts when slaughtering a sacrifice), and the qarin who misses Hajj (cuts when beginning the second tawaf). The passage then returns to the times of ramy, discussing the second time (recommended) and the fourth time (before sunrise and after sunset), which is restricted to those with excuse. It concludes with a report about the wording of takbir from various Companions, indicating that the phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the minimum, but additional phrases like 'raghman li-l-shaytan' are mentioned. Finally, the issue of standing for supplication is revisited, citing frequent narrations of the Prophet's action, and the restriction to the one in ihram for Hajj is noted as an attribution.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' (Allah is Greatest) with each pebble during ramy; a recommended sunnah act.
تلبية (talbiyah): The invocation 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk...' recited by pilgrims during ihram; it is to be cut off at specific points during the rites.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The largest of the three stone pillars in Mina; the first to be stoned on the Day of Nahr with seven pebbles.
مفرد (mufrid): A pilgrim performing Hajj only, without Umrah.
متمتع (mutamatti'): A pilgrim performing Umrah first, then Hajj with a break in between.
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim combining Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a mutamatti' (performing tamattu') cut the talbiyah?
A) When he begins the tawaf of Umrah
B) When he throws the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah
C) When he enters Mecca
D) When he begins the sa'y

Key Takeaway
Saying takbir with each pebble is sunnah, not wajib; cutting talbiyah is sunnah at the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah for all Hajj pilgrims.

Times for Stoning on the Day of Nahr and Tashriq Days
Determining the permissible, preferable, and disliked times for ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four possible time slots for ramy on the Day of Nahr and the days of Tashriq, identify which time is invalid by consensus, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the disliked times.

Core Idea
Ramy is invalid before dawn on the Day of Nahr; four time slots exist, with a Hanafi difference on the ruling for pre-sunrise and post-sunset.

The timing of ramy (stoning the jamarat) is crucial for the validity of this ritual. This lesson examines the permissible windows for ramy on the Day of Nahr and the following days of Tashriq, highlighting a subtle intra-Hanafi difference in classifying some of these times. Understanding these rules ensures your hajj rites are performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its temporal constraints
Ramy is wajib on the Day of Nahr and the days of Tashriq. The question is: during which hours can it be performed validly? The passage lists four time slots.
The act itself is stoning the three jamarat with pebbles.
2
List the four time slots mentioned
The passage enumerates: (1) after dawn but before sunrise (invalid before dawn by consensus), (2) from sunrise to zawal (noon), (3) from zawal to sunset, and (4) before sunrise and after sunset.
Note that slot 4 includes two separate periods: before sunrise (after dawn) and after sunset.
3
Understand the consensus on pre-dawn
The passage states that ramy before dawn of Yawm al-Nahr is not valid by consensus (ittifāqan). This is a firm ruling: no stoning before fajr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
This is based on the sunnah timing; the Prophet (ﷺ) stoned after sunrise.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on the fourth slot
The majority view (al-aktharūn) classifies the fourth slot as valid but makruh (disliked). However, in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, the author separates the 'permissible' time from the 'disliked', implying that only three slots are permissible while the fourth is disliked. This is a minor difference within the Hanafi school.
The 'first' opinion (al-awwal) is the majority view that all four slots are valid, but the fourth is makruh.
5
Recognize the practical implication
The practical difference is negligible: both views agree that ramy before sunrise and after sunset is valid but disliked. The dispute is only about whether to call it 'permissible' or keep it as a separate category. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the majority view.
The mufta bihi: stoning during the fourth slot is valid but makruh tanzihan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل طلوع فجر يوم النحر لم يصح اتفاقاً. والثاني من طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال. والثالث من الزوال إلى الغروب والرابع قبل طلوع الشمس وبعد الغروب كذا في المحيط وغيره. وجعل في الفتاوى الظهيرية الوقت المباح من المكروه فهي ثلاثة عنده، والأكثرون على الأول.
Before dawn of the Day of Nahr it is not valid by consensus. The second (time) from sunrise to zawal. The third from zawal to sunset. And the fourth before sunrise and after sunset. Thus in al-Muhit and other works. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, the permissible time is separated from the disliked, so they are three according to him, and the majority are upon the first (opinion).
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the times for ramy (stoning) on the Day of Nahr and the days of Tashriq. It states that it is not valid to stone before dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah by consensus. The second permissible time is from sunrise to zawal (noon), the third from zawal to sunset, and the fourth before sunrise and after sunset. The source references al-Muhit and others. However, in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, the permissible time is separated from the disliked times, making only three permissible times according to the author of that work. The majority of scholars follow the first opinion that all four times are valid but some are disliked. This reflects an intra-Hanafi difference regarding which times are makruh.

Key Terms
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.
الرمي (al-Ramy): The stoning of the jamarat by throwing pebbles.
الزوال (al-Zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., true noon.
أيام التشريق (Ayyām al-Tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is ramy invalid by consensus on the Day of Nahr?
A) After sunrise
B) Before dawn
C) After zawal
D) Between sunrise and zawal

Key Takeaway
The validity of ramy on the Day of Nahr depends on its timing; it is invalid before dawn, but valid in four time slots, with the fourth slot (before sunrise and after sunset) being disliked according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Takbir with Each Pebble During Ramy: Preferred Practice and Sufficiency
Ruling on saying the takbir when throwing each pebble

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on saying takbir when throwing pebbles during ramy, distinguish between the preferred (afdal) and sufficient (mujzi) forms, and explain the Hanafi position on du'a after stoning.

Core Idea
Takbir with each pebble is sunnah, not wajib; any dhikr or even silence suffices for validity.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the instruction 'say takbir with every pebble'. It explains that while takbir is the recommended practice, the obligation of ramy is fulfilled even if one says no dhikr or substitutes it with tahleel or tasbeeh. The author also addresses why the Prophet did not make du'a after stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, offering both a rule and a secondary reasoning based on harm prevention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its preferred level
The matn instructs to say takbir with each pebble. The commentator explains that this is a statement of preference (afdal), not an obligation. Determine the implied hukm level of the takbir.
The phrase 'li bayan al-afdal' is key.
2
Determine what suffices as an alternative
If the pilgrim does not mention Allah at all, or says tahleel ('La ilaha illa Allah') or tasbeeh ('Subhan Allah'), the ramy is still valid. Understand that the essence of ramy is the throwing, not a specific formula.
This shows takbir is not a condition (shart) or pillar (rukn).
3
Contrast the du'a ruling for different jamarat
The commentator gives a rule: stand for du'a after a jamrah only if another jamrah is to be stoned that same day. Since Jamrat al-Aqaba is the last, no du'a is performed there. Note the exception for the three jamarat on other days.
The rule is drawn from al-Zahiriyyah, but the commentator finds it problematic.
4
Analyze the commentator's critique
The commentator points out that du'a after completing worship is generally recommended (as in salah and sawm). He prefers to follow the Prophet's action (tark al-du'a) without seeking a rational reason, though he offers a possible wisdom: avoiding congestion at the road.
This illustrates Hanafi methodology of prioritizing action over analogy when a textual precedent exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكبر بكل حصاة أي مع كل حصاة من السبعة بيان للأفضل فلو لم يذكر الله أصلاً أو هلل أو سبح أجزأه ، ولم يذكر الدعاء آخره لأن السنة أن لا يقف عندها كما سيشير إليه في رمي الجمار الثلاث وضابطه أن كل جمرة بعدها جمرة فإنه يقف بعدها للدعاء لأنه في أثناء العبادة، وكل جمرة ليس بعدها جمرة ترمى في يومه لا يقف عندها لأنه خرج من العبادة. كذا في الظهيرية وهو مشكل فإن الدعاء بعد الخروج من العبادة مستحب كما في الصلاة والصوم إذا خرج منهما فالأولى الاستدلال بفعله عليه السلام كذلك وإن لم تظهر له حكمة، وقد يقال هي كون الوقوف يقع في جمرة العقبة في الطريق فيوجب قطع سلوكها على الناس وشدة ازدحام الواقفين والمارين ويفضي ذلك إلى ضرر عظيم بخلافه في باقي الجمرات فإنه لا يقع في نفس الطريق بل بمعزل عنه
His saying: 'And say the takbir with every pebble' i.e., with every one of the seven pebbles, an explanation of the preferred action. So if he does not mention Allah at all, or says 'La ilaha illa Allah' or 'Subhan Allah', it suffices. And he did not mention the du'a at the end because the sunnah is not to stand for du'a there, as he will indicate later in (the discussion of) stoning the three jamarat. The rule is: every jamrah after which there is another jamrah (to be stoned the same day), one stands for du'a because one is still in the act of worship. Every jamrah after which there is no other jamrah to be stoned that day, one does not stand for du'a because one has exited the act of worship. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah. But this is problematic because du'a after exiting an act of worship is recommended, as in prayer and fasting when one finishes them. So it is better to base it on his (the Prophet's) action, even if no reason is apparent. It may be said that the reason is that standing at Jamrat al-Aqaba occurs on the road, causing delay to people and severe crowding of those standing and passing, leading to great harm, unlike the other jamarat which are not on the main road but away from it.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn's instruction to say takbir with each pebble when stoning. It clarifies that the takbir is preferred (afdal); if one omits Allah's name entirely or says tahleel or tasbeeh, it is sufficient. The author then discusses the absence of du'a after Jamrat al-Aqaba. The rule is that one stands for du'a after a jamrah only if another jamrah follows that day (for the three jamarat on the first two days). Since Jamrat al-Aqaba is the last jamrah that day, one does not stand. The source al-Zahiriyyah states this, but the commentator notes a problem: du'a after completing worship is recommended in general (like after salah or sawm). He suggests following the Prophet's action literally, which he did not stand for du'a there. A possible reason is that standing at Jamrat al-Aqaba would block the road and cause crowding, unlike the other jamarat.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-Takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The largest jamarah, closest to Mina, stoned on the Day of Nahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Takbir with each pebble is sunnah, not obligatory; the essence of ramy is the act of throwing, and any dhikr or silence fulfills the obligation.
