When to Cut the Talbiyah During Hajj
Ruling on when to stop reciting the talbiyah for muhrims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact moment when the muhrim for Hajj cuts the talbiyah and distinguish the exceptions for the mu'tamir, muhsar, and those who miss Hajj.

Core Idea
The talbiyah is cut with the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqaba, not after all actions.

When performing Hajj, you recite the talbiyah as a sunnah. But when exactly should you stop? The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice, teaches that the talbiyah ends with the first pebble thrown at the largest jamarah. This lesson unpacks that ruling, including special cases for different types of pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The matn states: 'Cut the talbiyah with the first (pebble).' This means as soon as you throw your first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqaba, you cease reciting 'Labbayk…'
2
Recognize the dalil
The hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: 'He (peace be upon him) continued to recite the talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba.' This shows the stopping point is the commencement of stoning.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).
3
Distinguish the general rule from exceptions
The rule applies to all Hajj pilgrims (mufrid, mutamatti', qarin). But exceptions are made for: mu'tamir (cuts upon touching Black Stone), muhsar (cuts after slaughtering hady), and the one who misses Hajj (cuts when beginning tawaf for 'umrah).
These exceptions are based on the nature of their tahlul.
4
Expand with additional rulings
The talbiyah is also cut if any one of four actions on the Day of Nahr is done before stoning: shaving, tawaf al-ziyarah, slaughter of tamattu'/qiran, or the lapse of the preferred stoning time.
This is an extension from al-Muhit.

قوله : واقطع التلبية بأولها) أي مع أول حصاة ترميها لحديث الصحيحين: لم يزل عليه السلام يلبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة. ولا فرق بين المفرد والمتمتع والقارن وقيد بالمحرم بالحج لأن المعتمر يقطع التلبية إذا استلم الحجر لأن الطواف ركن في العمرة فيقطع التلبية قبل الشروع فيه، وقيد بكونه مدركاً للحج بإدراك الوقوف بعرفة لأن فائت الحج إذا تحلل بالعمرة يقطع التلبية حين يأخذ في الطواف لأن العمرة واجبة عليه فصار كالمعتمر والمحصر يقطعها إذا ذبح هديه لأن الذبح للتحلل، والقارن إذا كان فائت الحج يقطع حين يأخذ في الطواف الثاني لأنه يتحلل بعده. وأشار وعليه يحمل ما قدمناه عن الفتح تأمل قوله : (والثاني من طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال) قال الرملي : أي المستحب وقد وافق على الاستحباب العيني، وذكره في مجمع الرواية عن المحيط أيضاً بصيغة المسنون ووافقه في النهر قوله : (والرابع) قبل طلوع الشمس الخ) قيده في الفتح بعد أحاديث ساقها بعدم العذر قال : حتى لا يكون رمي الضعفة قبل الشمس ورمي الرعاة ليلاً يلزمهم الإساءة وكيف بذلك بعد الترخص قول المصنف : وكبر) بكل حصاة كذا روى ابن مسعود وابن جابر وأم سليمان، وظاهر المرويات من ذلك الاقتصار على «الله أكبر) غير أنه روى عن الحسن بن زياد أنه يقول الله أكبر رغماً للشيطان وخربه». وقيل يقول أيضاً اللهم اجعل حجي مبروراً وسعي مشكوراً وذنبي مغفوراً. كذا في الفتح قوله : ( فالأولى الاستدلال بفعله عليه الخ قال في الفتح : على هذا تظافرت الروايات عنه عليه السلام ولم يظهر حكمة تخصيص الوقوف والدعاء بغيرها من الجمرتين، فإن تخايل أنه في اليوم الأول لكثرة ما عليه من الشغل كالذبح والحلق والإفاضة إلى مكة فهو منعدم فيما بعده من الأيام قوله : ( وقيد بالمحرم بالحج) نسب إليه هذا التقييد وإن لم يكن مصرحاً به، وكذا ما بعده بكل حصاة واقطع التلبية بأولها ثم اذبح ثم احلق أو قصر والحلق أحب وحل لك كل بالرمي إلى أنه يقطعها إذا فعل واحداً من الأمور الأربعة التي تفعل في الحج يوم النحر فيقطعها إن حلق قبل الرمي أو طاف الزيارة قبل الرمي والذبح والحلق أو ذبح قبل الرمي دم التمتع أو القرآن ومضي وقت الرمي المستحب كفعله فيقطعها إذا لم يرم جمرة العقبة حتى زالت الشمس. كذا في المحيط
His saying: 'And cut the talbiyah with the first (pebble)' i.e., with the first pebble you throw, due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'He (peace be upon him) continued to recite the talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba.' There is no difference between the mufrid, mutamatti', and qarin. It is restricted to the muhrim for Hajj because the one performing 'umrah cuts the talbiyah when he touches the Black Stone since tawaf is a pillar in 'umrah, so he cuts the talbiyah before starting it. And it is restricted to one who has grasped Hajj by being present at 'Arafah because the one who misses Hajj and makes tahlul with 'umrah cuts the talbiyah when he begins tawaf because 'umrah is obligatory on him, so he becomes like the mu'tamir. The muhsar cuts it when he slaughters his hady because the slaughter is for tahlul. The qarin who has missed Hajj cuts when he begins the second tawaf because he makes tahlul after it. And it is indicated and upon it is based what we presented from al-Fath... [interruption] ... 'With every pebble and cut the talbiyah with the first (pebble), then slaughter, then shave or trim, and shaving is more beloved, and everything becomes permissible for you with the ramy (stoning) up to that he cuts it when he does one of the four things that are done in Hajj on the Day of Nahr: he cuts it if he shaves before stoning, or performs tawaf al-ziyarah before stoning, slaughter and shaving, or if he slaughters before stoning the blood of tamattu' or qiran, and the time of the preferred stoning passes, like his doing it, he cuts it if he does not stone Jamrat al-Aqaba until the sun has set. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's instruction to cut the talbiyah with the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqaba. It cites the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim that the Prophet continued reciting talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. The ruling applies to all types of pilgrims (mufrid, mutamatti', qarin). However, the rule is specifically for the one in ihram for Hajj, not 'umrah, because the mu'tamir cuts talbiyah upon touching the Black Stone. Similarly, exceptions are made for those who miss Hajj and perform tahlul with 'umrah, for the muhsar (prevented from completing Hajj), and for the qarin who misses Hajj. The text then appends a list from al-Muhit: the talbiyah is also cut if one performs any one of the four actions on the Day of Nahr before stoning (shaving, tawaf al-ziyarah, slaughter of tamattu'/qiran, or the lapse of the preferred time for stoning).

Key Terms
التلبية (al-Talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' by the muhrim.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The largest jamarah, stoned on the Day of Nahr.
المحصر (al-Muhsar): One prevented from completing Hajj by enemies or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the mufrid (individual) pilgrim cut the talbiyah?
A) With the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqaba
B) After completing stoning all three jamarat
C) Upon entering Mecca
D) After shaving or trimming

Key Takeaway
The talbiyah ends with the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqaba, based on the sunnah of the Prophet.

The Ruling on Shaving and Shortening in Hajj: Obligation, Minimum, and Sunnah
Expanding on the order of actions and rulings on shaving/shortening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on halaq and taqsir, identify the minimum required amount (rub' al-ra's), and explain the preferred sequence of actions on Yawm al-Nahr and the sunan of shaving.

Core Idea
Shaving or shortening is wajib; shaving is more virtuous, both require at least a quarter of the head.

On the Day of Sacrifice, the pilgrim performs ramy, then sacrifice (for qarin/mutamatti), then shaves or shortens. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that halaq/taqsir is a wajib act of Hajj, not a rukn, and details the minimum amount, exceptions for baldness or sores, and the sunan including starting from the right side. Understanding these details ensures proper tahlul and avoids invalidating one's Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred order
The text states the preferred sequence: ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah, then sacrifice (if applicable), then shave or shorten. However, if done out of order, tahlul still occurs after halaq/taqsir.
Talbiyah is cut with the first stone of ramy, but if halaq occurs before ramy, talbiyah is cut at halaq.
2
Define the wajib act and its amount
Halaq means removing hair from at least a quarter of the head. Taqsir means taking from each hair (of at least a quarter of the head) about a finger joint's length.
If bald: run razor over head. If sores: obligation drops. Not finding tools is not an excuse.
3
Analyze the virtue of shaving
The Prophet prayed for mercy three times for those who shave, and once for those who shorten, making shaving more virtuous.
Hadith from the Two Sahihs: 'أَخَذَ وَأَشَارَ إِلَى الْجَانِبِ الْأَيْمَنِ' also shows starting with right side is sunnah.
4
Recognize the sunan of shaving
Start from the right side of the head (contrary to common Hanafi practice of left side, but Fath al-Qadir confirms right side as correct). Bury hair, make supplication and takbir. Use a razor. Trim nails and mustache after, but not beard.
Throwing hair in toilet or bath is makruh.
5
Apply exceptions
If shaving is impossible due to disease (sores on head), the obligation drops and tahlul occurs as if shaved. Likewise if no tool/barber is found, it is not an excuse because tools can be obtained.
The text distinguishes between temporary obstacles (tool) and permanent (sores).

بكل حصاة واقطع التلبية بأولها ثم اذبح ثم احلق أو قصر والحلق أحب وحل لك كل بالرمي إلى أنه يقطعها إذا فعل واحداً من الأمور الأربعة التي تفعل في الحج يوم النحر فيقطعها إن حلق قبل الرمي أو طاف الزيارة قبل الرمي والذبح والحلق أو ذبح قبل الرمي دم التمتع أو القرآن ومضي وقت الرمي المستحب كفعله فيقطعها إذا لم يرم جمرة العقبة حتى زالت الشمس. كذا في المحيط قوله : (ثم اذبح) أي على وجه الأفضلية لأن الكلام في المفرد وهو ليس بواجب عليه وإنما يجب على القارن والمتمتع، وأما الأضحية فإن كان مسافراً فلا أضحية عليه وإلا فعليه كالمكي، وقد ثبت في حديث جابر الطويل أنه عليه السلام ذبح بيده وستين بدنة وأمر علياً فذبح ما بقي وأشركه في هديه ثم أمر من كل بدنة ببضعة فجعلت في قدر فطبخت فأكلا من لحمها وشربا من مرقها ثم ركب إلى البيت فصلى بمكة الظهر. قال ابن حبان والحكمة في أنه لنحر ثلاثاً وستين بدنة أنه ان له يومئذ ثلاث وستون سنة فنحر لكل سنة بدنة . ثلاثاً قوله : (ثم احلق أو قصر والحلق أحب بيان للواجب والمراد بالحلق إزالة شعر ربع الرأس إن أمكن وإلا بأن كان أقرع فيجري الموسى على رأسه إن أمكن وأحب على المختار وإلا بأن كان على رأسه قروح لا يمكن إمرار الموسى عليه ولا يصل إلى تقصيره فقط سقط هذا الواجب وحل كمن حلقها. والأحسن أن يؤخر الإحلال إلى آخر الوقت من أيام النحر، ولو أمكنه الحلق لكن لم يجد آلة ولا من يحلقها فليس بعذر وليس له الإحلال لأن إصابة الآلة مرجو كل ساعة ولا كذلك برء القروح واندمالها والإزالة لا تختص بالموسى بل بأي آلة كانت أو بالنورة، والمستحب الحلق بالموسى لأن السنة وردت به والمراد بالتقصير أن يأخذ الرجل أو المرأة من رؤوس شعر ربع الرأس مقدار الأنملة كذا ذكر الشارح. ومراده أن يأخذ من كل شعرة مقدار الأنملة كما صرح به في المحيط. وفي البدائع قالوا: يجب أن يزيد في التقصير على قدر الأنملة حتى يستوفي قدر الأنملة من كل شعرة برأسه لأن أطراف الشعر غير متساو عادة. قال الحلبي في مناسكه : وهو حسن والأنملة بفتح الهمزة والميم وضم الميم لغة مشهورة ومن خطأ راويها فقد أخطأ واحدة .الأنامل . ثم التخيير بين الحلق والتقصير العذر فلو تعذر الحلق لعارض تعين التقصير أو التقصير تعين الحلق كأن هو عدم لبدة بصمغ فلا يعمل فيه المقراض، وإنما كان الحلق أفضل لدعائه عليه السلام للمحلقين بالرحمة ثنتين أو ثلاثاً وفي الثالثة أو الرابعة للمقصرين بها. ويستحب حلق الكل للإتباع. ولم يذكر سنن الحلق لأنه لا يخص الحلق في الحج لأن أصل الحلق في كل جمعة مستحب كما صرح به في القنية، ويعتبر في سنته البداءة باليمين للحالق لا المحلوق فيبدأ بشقه الأيسر، إنما . عند لأن الكلام فيه فهو مما تضمنه كلامه قوله: (ومراده أن يأخذ من كل شعرة الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية قلت: يظهر لي أن المراد بكل شعرة أي من شعر الربع على وجه اللزوم أو من الكل على سبيل ويستحب ومقتضى النص البداءة بيمين الرأس لما في الصحيحين أنه عليه السلام قال للحلاق خذ وأشار إلى الجانب الأيمن ثم الأيسر ثم جعل يعطيه الناس وفي فتح القدير : إنه هو الصواب وهو خلاف ما ذكر في المذهب. ويستحب دفن شعره والدعاء عند الحلق وبعد الفراغ مع التكبير وإن رمى الشعر فلا بأس به وكره إلقاؤه في الكنيف والمغتسل. كذا في فتاوى العلامي. له أن يقص أظفاره وشواربه بعد الحلق للإتباع ولا يأخذ من لحيته شيئاً لأنه مثلة ولو فعل لا يلزمه شيء
With every pebble and cut the talbiyah at its first, then sacrifice, then shave or shorten, and shaving is more beloved, and everything becomes permissible for you with the ramy... until he cuts it when he does one of the four things done in Hajj on the Day of Sacrifice: he cuts it if he shaves before ramy, or performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah before ramy, sacrifice, and shaving, or sacrifices before ramy the blood of tamattu' or qiran, and the preferred time for ramy passes like its performance: he cuts it if he does not throw at Jamrat al-Aqabah until the sun has passed its zenith. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: (then sacrifice) i.e. as a matter of preference, because the speech concerns the mufrid, and sacrifice is not obligatory upon him; it is only obligatory upon the qarin and mutamatti'. As for the udhiyah, if he is a traveler there is no udhiyah upon him; otherwise it is upon him like the Makkan. It has been established in the long hadith of Jabir that he (peace be upon him) sacrificed with his own hand sixty-three badanas and ordered Ali to sacrifice the remainder and made him a partner in his offering, then ordered a piece from each badana to be placed in a pot, cooked, and they ate of its meat and drank of its broth, then he rode to the House and prayed Zuhr in Makkah. Ibn Hibban said: The wisdom in his sacrificing sixty-three badanas is that he was sixty-three years old that day, so he sacrificed a badana for each year. His statement: (then shave or shorten, and shaving is more beloved) is an explanation of the obligatory. What is meant by shaving is removing the hair of a quarter of the head if possible; otherwise, if he is bald, he runs the razor over his head if possible, and it is more beloved according to the chosen view; otherwise, if there are sores on his head such that the razor cannot be passed over it and he cannot even shorten it, this obligation drops and he becomes permissible like one who has shaved. It is better to delay the tahlul to the end of the time of the Days of Sacrifice. If he can shave but does not find a tool or someone to shave him, that is not an excuse and he does not become permissible, because obtaining the tool is hoped for every hour, unlike the healing of sores. Removal is not specific to a razor but with any tool or with depilatory. It is recommended to shave with a razor because the Sunnah came with it. What is meant by shortening is that a man or woman takes from the hair of the head a quarter of the head the length of a finger joint; thus the commentator mentioned. His intent is that he takes from each hair the length of a finger joint, as clarified in al-Muhit. In al-Bada'i' they said: One must increase in shortening beyond the measure of a finger joint so that the full finger joint length is fulfilled from each hair of his head, because the ends of hair are usually uneven. Al-Halabi said in his Manasik: This is good. Al-Anmulah (finger joint) is commonly pronounced with fathah on the hamzah and mim and with damm on the mim, and whoever criticizes the narrator has erred. Then the choice between shaving and shortening is an excuse: if shaving is not possible due to an obstacle, shortening becomes obligatory; or if shortening is not possible, shaving becomes obligatory, like when there is a lock of hair hardened with gum so scissors do not work on it. Shaving is better because he (peace be upon him) prayed for mercy for those who shave two or three times, and on the third or fourth time for those who shorten. It is recommended to shave all of the head for following the Sunnah. He did not mention the sunan of shaving because it is not specific to shaving in Hajj; the basic principle of shaving every Friday is recommended as clarified in al-Qunyah. In its sunnah it is considered to begin with the right side for the shaver, not the shaved one, so he begins with his left side. Because the speech is about it, and this is what his words include. His statement: (and his intent that he takes from each hair etc.) He said in al-Sharnabaliyyah: I say: It appears to me that what is meant by each hair means from the hair of the quarter as a matter of necessity, or from all as a matter of recommendation. And recommended, and the apparent meaning of the text is beginning with the right side of the head, because in the two Sahihs he (peace be upon him) said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to the right side, then the left, then he gave it to the people. In Fath al-Qadir: That is correct, contrary to what is mentioned in the school. It is recommended to bury his hair and make supplication at the time of shaving and after finishing with takbir. If he throws away the hair there is no harm, but it is disliked to throw it in the toilet or bath. Thus in the Fatawa of al-Allami. He may trim his nails and mustache after shaving for following the Sunnah, and he should not take anything from his beard because it is mutilation, and if he does, nothing is required of him.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the order of actions on Yawm al-Nahr (the Day of Sacrifice) and the rulings on shaving (halaq) and shortening (taqsir). The commentary begins by discussing when to cut off the talbiyah: it is cut with the first stone of ramy at Jamrat al-Aqabah. However, if one performs any of the four actions (ramy, dhbah, halaq, tawaf) out of order, the talbiyah is cut at the first of these that is done. The preferred order is ramy, then dhabh, then halaq. The author then clarifies that the command to sacrifice (dhabh) is on the basis of preference (afdaliyyah) for the mufrid (one performing Hajj Ifrad), as sacrifice is not obligatory for him; it is only obligatory for the qarin (performing Qiran) and mutamatti' (Tamattu'). For the udhiyah (sacrificial animal of 'Eid), a traveler is not obliged, but a resident is. A hadith from Jabir is cited about the Prophet's own sacrifice. The passage then defines the obligation of shaving or shortening: shaving means removing hair from at least a quarter of the head; if bald, the razor is passed over the head; if there are sores preventing shaving, the obligation drops. The preferred time for tahlul (partial release from ihram) is the last day of the Days of Sacrifice. Not finding a tool or barber is not an excuse. Shortening is defined as taking from each hair of a quarter of the head about a finger joint's length, with a recommendation to take a bit more to ensure each hair is shortened. The virtue of shaving over shortening is proven by the hadith where the Prophet prayed for mercy three times for those who shave and once for those who shorten. The sunan of shaving are then discussed: beginning with the right side of the head (according to the correct view, contrary to what is in the Hanafi school as stated in Fath al-Qadir), burying the hair, making supplication, and not taking from the beard.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halaq): Shaving the head, specifically at least a quarter of the head as a wajib act of Hajj.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Shortening the hair, taking about a finger joint's length from each hair of at least a quarter of the head.
الإحلال (al-ihlal): The release from ihram; partial ihlal occurs with halaq/taqsir (allowing perfume etc.), full ihlal occurs after tawaf al-ziyarah (allowing women).
الأنملة (al-anmulah): The finger joint, a measurement for the length of hair to be shortened.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of hair that must be removed for halaq (shaving) to be valid in the Hanafi school?
A) The entire head
B) At least one hair
C) At least a quarter of the head
D) At least half the head

Key Takeaway
Halaq or taqsir is a wajib act of Hajj requiring at least a quarter of the head; shaving is more virtuous, and the preferred order is ramy, then dhabh (if applicable), then halaq.

The Two Stages of Tahlul: Perfume After Ramy? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Clarifying the two stages of tahlul and the intra-Hanafi dispute on perfume after ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two stages of tahlul in Hajj according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether ramy alone permits perfume.

Core Idea
Ramy does not cause tahlul; only shaving releases prohibitions – perfume is permitted only after halaq, not after ramy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a crucial question: when does a pilgrim become partially released from ihram? The matn states that after shaving, everything becomes permissible except women. But a minority view attributed to Abu Yusuf and found in Fatawa Qadikhan suggests that after ramy, perfume is already permissible. The commentator Ibn Nujaym refutes this, defending the established Hanafi position that only shaving (or shortening) triggers the first tahlul. We will explore the evidence and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two stages of tahlul
Distinguish the first tahlul (by shaving/taqsir) from the second (by tawaf al-ziyarah). The first lifts all prohibitions except women; the second lifts the prohibition of women.
This is the established Hanafi doctrine (Zahir al-Riwayah).
2
Locate the mainstream Hanafi ruling on ramy
According to al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, ramy is not a cause of tahlul. All prohibitions remain until shaving.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi opposing view
In Fatawa Qadikhan, it is reported that after ramy but before shaving, everything is permissible except perfume and women. A narration from Abu Yusuf permits even perfume.
This creates a conflict within the school that requires resolution.
4
Analyze the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Aisha (she perfumed the Prophet at his tahlul, after shaving) proves perfume is permitted after shaving. Also, perfume is a motivator to intercourse, so it cannot be permitted before the act that permits women (tawaf).
The dalil is clear and supports the mainstream view.
5
Understand the tarjih and mufta bihi
Ibn Nujaym deems the view in Fatawa Qadikhan weak, citing inconsistency and the stronger evidence. The mufta bihi is that no tahlul occurs by ramy; perfume and women remain forbidden until shaving and tawaf respectively.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah; supported by al-Mabsut, al-Muhit.

Source Text

قوله : (وحل لك غير النساء أي بالحلق ) أي فحل التطيب لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها في الصحيحين قالت : طيبت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لحله حين أحل ولحله حين أحرم. وحرم الدواعي كالوطء أفاد أنه ليس قبل الحلق تحليل لشيء مما كان حلالاً بالإحرام ويدل عليه ما في المبسوط. فالحاصل أن في الحج إحلالين : أحدهما بالحلق والثاني بالطواف وما في الهداية وغيرها من أن الرمي ليس من أسباب التحلل عندنا يخالفه ما في فتاوى قاضيخان ولفظه : وبعد الرمي قبل الحلق يحل له كل شيء إلا الطيب والنساء. وعن أبي يوسف يحل له الطيب أيضاً وإن كان لا يحل له النساء، والصحيح ما قلنا لأن الطيب داع إلى الجماع وإنما عرفنا حل الطيب بعد الحلق قبل طواف الزيادة بالأثر ا هـ . وينبغي أن يحكم بضعف ما في الفتاوى لما قدمنا ولما في المحيط ولفظه : ولو أبيح له التحلل فغسل رأسه بالخطمي وقلم ظفره قبل الحلق فعليه لأن الإحرام باق لأنه لا يحل إلا بالحلق فقد جنى عليه، وقد ذكر الطحاوي لا دم عليه عند أبي يوسف ومحمد دم أنه هو الأولوية، فلا مخالفة في الإجزاء لأن الربع كالكل كما في الحلق قوله : (وفي فتح القدير الصواب) قال في النهر : ويوافقه ما في الملتقط عن الإمام حلقت رأسي بمكة فخطأني الحلاق في ثلاثة أشياء : لما أن جلست قال استقبل القبلة وناولته الجانب الأيسر فقال ابدأ بالأيمن، فلما أردت أن أذهب قال ادفن شعرك فرجعت فدفنته ا هـ قلت: وفي المعراج روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام حلق رأسه من يمين الحالق وعن الشافعي من يمين المحلوق فاعتبرنا يمين الحالق وهو يمين المحلوق . قال الكرماني : ذكره بعض أصحابنا ولم يعزه إلى أحد بل الأولى اتباع السنة فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بدأ بيمينه في الصحيح، وقد أخذ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقول الحجام حين قال ادن الشق الأيمن من رأسك وفيه حكاية معروفة | هـ. وهذا أيضاً يؤيد ما استصوبه في الفتح ويفيد أن خلافه ليس مما ثبت عند أهل المذهب قوله : ( وينبغي أن يحكم بضعف ما في الفتاوى) قال في الشرنبلالية أقول : لم يقتصر قاضيخان على ما نقله عنه في البحر لأنه نص على ما يوافق الهداية أيضاً قبل هذا بقوله : والخروج عن الإحرام إنما يكون بالحلق أو التقصير فإذا خلق أو قصر حل له كل شيء إلا النساء ما لم يطف بالبيت ؛ مروي ذلك عن عائشة رضي الله عنها عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. وبعد الرمي قبل الحلق يحل له كل شيء إلا الطيب والنساء، وعن أبي يوسف يحل له الطيب
His statement: (and everything becomes permissible for you except women, i.e., by shaving) i.e., perfume becomes permissible based on the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) in the two Sahihs: she said, 'I perfumed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for his tahlul when he performed tahlul and for his ihram when he assumed ihram.' And the causes (like intercourse) are forbidden. It indicates that before shaving there is no tahlul for anything that was prohibited by ihram. This is supported by what is in al-Mabsut. The conclusion is that in Hajj there are two stages of tahlul: one by shaving and the second by tawaf. What is in al-Hidayah and others that ramy is not among the causes of tahlul in our school is contradicted by what is in Fatawa Qadikhan, whose wording: 'After ramy but before shaving, everything becomes permissible for him except perfume and women. And from Abu Yusuf: perfume also becomes permissible for him, although women do not.' The correct view is what we said, because perfume is a motivator to intercourse, and we only know the permissibility of perfume after shaving before Tawaf al-Ziyadah through athar. It is appropriate to rule that the view in the Fatawa is weak due to what we presented and because of what is in al-Muhit, whose wording: 'If it were permitted for him to do tahlul, then he washed his head with khitmi and trimmed his nail before shaving, he owes something because the ihram remains, since he is only released by shaving, so he has violated it.' And al-Tahawi mentioned: There is no blood (dam) upon him according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Then the text returns to the earlier discussion: 'It is a matter of priority, so there is no contradiction in sufficiency because the quarter is like the whole, as in shaving.' Then: 'In Fath al-Qadir, the correct view is...' He said in al-Nahr: It is supported by what is in al-Multaqat from the Imam: 'I shaved my head in Makkah and the barber made three mistakes with me: When I sat down he said face the qiblah, and I handed him the left side, and he said start with the right; when I wanted to leave he said bury your hair, and I returned and buried it.' I say: In al-Mi'raj it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved his head from the right side of the shaver, and according to al-Shafi'i from the right side of the shaved one, so we considered the right side of the shaver, which is the right side of the shaved one. Al-Kirmani said: Some of our companions mentioned it without attributing it to anyone, but rather following the Sunnah is better, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) began with his right side in the Sahih. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) took the statement of the cupper when he said: 'Bring the right side of your head closer,' and there is a well-known story about it. This also supports what was deemed correct in al-Fath and indicates that the opposite is not established among the people of the school. Then: 'It is appropriate to rule that what is in the Fatawa is weak.' He said in al-Sharnabaliyyah: I say: Qadikhan did not limit himself to what is transmitted from him in al-Bahr, because he also stated what agrees with al-Hidayah before this, saying: 'Exiting from ihram is only by shaving or shortening; so when he shaves or shortens, everything becomes permissible for him except women until he performs tawaf of the House.' This is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) from the Prophet (peace be upon him). 'And after ramy before shaving, everything becomes permissible for him except perfume and women. And from Abu Yusuf: perfume becomes permissible.'
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a critical refinement of the matn statement 'وحل لك غير النساء' (and everything becomes permissible for you except women). The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains that this tahlul is achieved by shaving (or shortening), not by ramy. He cites the hadith of Aisha that she perfumed the Prophet at the time of his tahlul, indicating that perfume is permissible after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The passage then addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school: the widely accepted view (as in al-Hidayah) is that ramy alone does not cause any tahlul; all prohibitions remain until shaving. However, in Fatawa Qadikhan, it is reported that after ramy but before shaving, everything except perfume and women is permissible, and from Abu Yusuf that even perfume is permissible. Ibn Nujaym argues that the correct view is the first, because perfume is a motivator to intercourse, and the permission for perfume after shaving is established by athar (tradition). He further supports this by citing al-Muhit: if tahlul were permitted before shaving, then washing the head with khitmi or trimming nails before shaving would incur a dam because ihram remains. The discussion also touches on the proper side to start shaving, reinforcing that the right side is correct based on the practice of the Prophet and a report from Abu Hanifa. The Sharnabaliyyah commentary defends Qadikhan by showing that he also stated the standard view elsewhere.

Key Terms
التحلل (al-tahlul): Release from the prohibitions of ihram; partial by shaving, complete by tawaf al-ziyarah.
الطيب (al-tib): Perfume; it becomes permissible after shaving (first tahlul) but before tawaf, according to the correct Hanafi view.
فتاوى قاضيخان (Fatawa Qadikhan): A collection of fatawa by Imam Qadikhan (d. 592 AH), containing some views that differ from the established madhhab, such as permissibility of perfume after ramy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position in this passage, when does perfume become permissible for a pilgrim performing Hajj?
A) After ramy at Jamrat al-Aqabah
B) After shaving (halaq) or shortening (taqsir)
C) After tawaf al-ziyarah
D) After both shaving and tawaf

Key Takeaway
Ramy is not a cause of tahlul; only shaving (halaq/taqsir) releases the pilgrim from most ihram prohibitions, including the prohibition of perfume.

Sunan of Shaving the Head (Halq) in Hajj
Lists and explains the sunan of halq with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) of shaving the head during Hajj and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes starting with the right side and burying the hair as sunan of halq.

Shaving the head (halq) or trimming (taqsir) is a wajib act that achieves the first tahallul in Hajj. However, there are several recommended practices (sunan) that a pilgrim should observe, such as beginning with the right side and making supplication. These sunan are derived from the Prophet's own actions and instructions. This lesson covers those sunan and the minor difference of opinion regarding the starting side.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act being discussed is shaving the head (halq) or trimming during Hajj. Note that halq is one of the causes of the first tahallul, which permits everything except women.
The source mentions halq in the context of tahallul.
2
List the sunan
From the passage, extract the recommended acts: starting with the right side, burying the hair, making supplication and takbir, cutting nails and mustache, and not cutting the beard. Note that throwing the hair is permissible but disliked in lavatories.
These sunan are based on hadith and athar.
3
Examine the evidence
The source cites the hadith in Sahihayn where the Prophet pointed to the right side first. Also, a story from al-Multaqat supports starting with the right.
The Fath al-Qadir deems this the correct view, contrary to some madhhab statements.
4
Note the difference on the starting side
There is a minor ikhtilaf: some say start from the barber's right, others from the shaved person's right. The sunna is to start with the right side of the shaved person, as the Prophet did.
The passage resolves this by referencing Abu Hanifa's practice.

كتاب الحج باب الإحرام ويستحب ومقتضى النص البداءة بيمين الرأس لما في الصحيحين أنه عليه السلام قال للحلاق خذ وأشار إلى الجانب الأيمن ثم الأيسر ثم جعل يعطيه الناس وفي فتح القدير : إنه هو الصواب وهو خلاف لأن الطيب داع إلى الجماع وإنما عرفنا حل الطيب بعد الحلق قبل طواف الزيادة بالأثر ا هـ . وينبغي أن يحكم بضعف ما في الفتاوى لما قدمنا ولما في المحيط ولفظه : ولو أبيح له التحلل فغسل رأسه بالخطمي وقلم ظفره قبل الحلق فعليه لأن الإحرام باق لأنه لا يحل إلا بالحلق فقد جنى عليه، وقد ذكر الطحاوي لا دم عليه عند أبي يوسف ومحمد دم أنه هو الأولوية، فلا مخالفة في الإجزاء لأن الربع كالكل كما في الحلق قوله : (وفي فتح القدير الصواب) قال في النهر : ويوافقه ما في الملتقط عن الإمام حلقت رأسي بمكة فخطأني الحلاق في ثلاثة أشياء : لما أن جلست قال استقبل القبلة وناولته الجانب الأيسر فقال ابدأ بالأيمن، فلما أردت أن أذهب قال ادفن شعرك فرجعت فدفنته ا هـ قلت: وفي المعراج روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام حلق رأسه من يمين الحالق وعن الشافعي من يمين المحلوق فاعتبرنا يمين الحالق وهو يمين المحلوق . قال الكرماني : ذكره بعض أصحابنا ولم يعزه إلى أحد بل الأولى اتباع السنة فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بدأ بيمينه في الصحيح، وقد أخذ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقول الحجام حين قال ادن الشق الأيمن من رأسك وفيه حكاية معروفة | هـ. وهذا أيضاً يؤيد ما استصوبه في الفتح ويفيد أن خلافه ليس مما ثبت عند أهل المذهب قوله : ( وينبغي أن يحكم بضعف ما في الفتاوى) قال في الشرنبلالية أقول : لم يقتصر قاضيخان على ما نقله عنه في البحر لأنه نص على ما يوافق الهداية أيضاً قبل هذا بقوله : والخروج عن الإحرام إنما يكون بالحلق أو التقصير فإذا خلق أو قصر حل له كل شيء إلا النساء ما لم يطف بالبيت ؛ مروي ذلك عن عائشة رضي الله عنها عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. وبعد الرمي قبل الحلق يحل له كل شيء إلا الطيب والنساء، وعن أبي يوسف يحل له الطيب شيء غير النساء ثم إلى مكة يوم النحر أو غداً أو بعده فطف للركن سبعة أشواط بلا لأنه أبيح له التحلل فيقع به التحلل ا هـ. فلو كان التحلل بالرمي حاصلاً في غير الطيب والنساء لم يلزمه دم بتقليم الأظفار وتخريجه على قول الطحاوي عندهما بعيد كما لا يخفى.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: It is recommended (mustahab) and the requirement of the text is to begin with the right side of the head because of what is in the Two Sahihs that he (peace be upon him) said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to the right side, then the left, then he began to give it to the people. And in Fath al-Qadir: That is the correct view, and it contradicts what is mentioned in the madhhab. It is recommended to bury his hair, to make supplication at the time of shaving and after finishing with takbir, and if he throws the hair there is no harm, and it is disliked to throw it in a lavatory or washroom. Thus in Fatawa al-Alami. He may cut his nails and mustache after shaving following the sunna, and he should not take anything from his beard because it is mutilation, and if he does nothing is required of him. His statement: (And what is other than women is permissible for you), meaning by shaving, so perfume is permissible because of the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) in the Two Sahihs: she said, 'I perfumed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he entered ihram and when he exited ihram before he circumambulated the House.' And the motives such as intercourse are forbidden. It indicates that before shaving there is no permission for anything that was forbidden by ihram, and this is supported by what is in al-Mabsut. The conclusion is that in Hajj there are two tahalluls: one by shaving and the second by tawaf. And what is in al-Hidayah and others that ramy is not one of the causes of tahallul with us is contradicted by what is in Fatawa Qadikhan, and his wording: 'After ramy before shaving, everything is permissible for him except perfume and women.' And from Abu Yusuf: perfume is also permissible for him, even though women are not permissible. The correct is what we said, because perfume motivates intercourse, and we have only known the permissibility of perfume after shaving before Tawaf al-Ziyadah by tradition (athar). It is necessary to judge the weakness of what is in the Fatawa due to what we presented and due to what is in al-Muhit: 'If tahallul were permitted to him, then he washed his head with khitmi and trimmed his nail before shaving, a blood (dam) is due because ihram remains as it is only removed by shaving, so he has violated it.' And al-Tahawi mentioned that there is no dam upon him according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. That [blood] is the priority, so there is no contradiction in sufficiency because a quarter is like the whole as in shaving. His statement: (And in Fath al-Qadir the correct view) said in al-Nahr: It is supported by what is in al-Multaqat from the Imam: 'I shaved my head in Makkah, and the barber made mistakes in three things: when I sat down, he said face the qibla; I handed him the left side, he said start with the right; when I wanted to go, he said bury your hair, so I returned and buried it.' I said: And in al-Mi'raj it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved his head from the right side of the barber, and from al-Shafi'i from the right side of the shaved person, so we consider the right of the barber which is the right of the shaved person. Al-Kirmani said: Some of our companions mentioned it and did not attribute it to anyone, but the first is to follow the sunna, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) began with his right in the Sahih, and Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) took the saying of the cupper when he said: 'Bring the right side of your head near,' and there is a well-known story. This also supports what was deemed correct in al-Fath and indicates that its disagreement is not established among the people of the madhhab. His statement: (And it is necessary to judge the weakness of what is in the Fatawa) said in al-Sharnabaliyya: I say: Qadikhan did not limit himself to what was transmitted from him in al-Bahr, because he also stated what agrees with al-Hidayah before this with his saying: 'And exiting ihram is only by shaving or trimming, so if he shaves or trims, everything is permissible for him except women as long as he has not circumambulated the House'; that is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) from the Prophet (may peace be upon him). And after ramy before shaving, everything is permissible for him except perfume and women. And from Abu Yusuf, perfume is permissible for him. Something other than women, then to Makkah on the Day of Nahr or the next day or after it, and circumambulate the pillar seven circuits without [saying] because tahallul was permitted for him, so tahallul occurs by it. If tahallul by ramy had occurred in other than perfume and women, then trimming nails would not necessitate a dam, and its derivation based on the saying of al-Tahawi with them is far-fetched, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the rulings related to shaving the head (halq) during Hajj and the associated legal dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding when perfume (tayyib) becomes permissible for the muhrim. The passage first addresses the recommended (mustahab) practice of beginning the shave from the right side of the head, citing the hadith in the Sahihayn where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed the barber to start with the right side. It then discusses other sunan: burying the hair, making dua and takbir, and the prohibition against cutting the beard. The core legal issue is the timing of tahallul (partial release from ihram). According to the Hanafi school, there are two tahalluls: the first occurs by shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir), which permits everything except women (i.e., sexual relations). The second occurs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which permits women. The text refutes the view found in Fatawa Qadikhan that after ramy (stoning) before halq, everything except perfume and women is permissible. It also reports Abu Yusuf's view that perfume becomes permissible after ramy. The correct Hanafi position, affirmed by the author, is that perfume is only permissible after halq, not after ramy, based on the hadith of Aisha that she perfumed the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he exited ihram before Tawaf, and the principle that perfume is a motivator for intercourse (dā'ī ilā al-jimā‘). The passage also includes a discussion of the beginning side of shaving, with a story from al-Multaqat and a reference to the Fath al-Qadir, concluding that starting with the right is the sunna. Finally, it addresses the issue of whether a dam (blood sacrifice) is required if one washes or trims nails before halq, and cites al-Tahawi's view that there is no dam according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but the preferred position is that a dam is due because ihram remains. The commentary ends by judging the view in Fatawa Qadikhan as weak, citing a contradiction within Qadikhan's own statements.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head completely, which is one of the ways to achieve the first tahallul in Hajj.
المثلة (al-muthla): Mutilation, disfigurement. In this context, cutting the beard is considered muthla and is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a sunan of shaving the head during Hajj?
A) Starting with the right side
B) Burying the hair
C) Cutting the beard
D) Making supplication and takbir

Key Takeaway
The sunan of halq include starting with the right, burying hair, making dua, and cutting nails, while beard cutting is prohibited as mutilation.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on When Perfume Becomes Permissible
Analyses the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the permissibility of perfume after ramy vs after halq, with tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when perfume becomes halal after ramy and halq, and evaluate the conflicting views within the madhhab.

Core Idea
Perfume becomes halal only after shaving (halq), not after stoning (ramy), because perfume motivates intercourse.

After the Day of Arafah, pilgrims perform ramy (stoning) and then halq (shaving). A key question is when perfume becomes permissible. The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that perfume becomes halal only after halq, not after ramy. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute, with Abu Yusuf permitting it after ramy, and a statement in Fatawa Qadikhan that after ramy everything except perfume and women is halal. This lesson dissects the evidence and tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is: at what point does perfume (tayyib) become permissible for a muhrim after the Day of Arafah? Is it after ramy (stoning) or after halq (shaving)?
Perfume was prohibited during ihram.
2
State the Hanafi principle of tahallul
According to the Hanafi school, there are two tahalluls: first by halq (permits everything except women), second by Tawaf al-Ziyarah (permits women). Ramy is not a cause of tahallul.
This is the basis of the dispute.
3
Compare the conflicting views
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: perfume halal only after halq. Abu Yusuf: perfume halal after ramy. Qadikhan's Fatawa: after ramy, everything except perfume and women is halal (i.e., perfume still haram). Identify each position from the passage.
Qadikhan's view contradicts his own earlier statement that tahallul is only by halq.
4
Analyze the evidence
The hadith of Aisha (Sahihayn) is cited: she perfumed the Prophet when he exited ihram before Tawaf, implying after halq. Also, the principle: perfume motivates intercourse, so it cannot be permitted while women are forbidden.
This evidence is considered stronger.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author declares the view that perfume is only halal after halq as 'sahih' (correct) and judges Qadikhan's statement as weak. The mufta bihi is that perfume is halal only after halq.
The discussion about nail trimming and dam also supports this tarjih.

كتاب الحج باب الإحرام ويستحب ومقتضى النص البداءة بيمين الرأس لما في الصحيحين أنه عليه السلام قال للحلاق خذ وأشار إلى الجانب الأيمن ثم الأيسر ثم جعل يعطيه الناس وفي فتح القدير : إنه هو الصواب وهو خلاف قال ادفن شعرك فرجعت فدفنته ا هـ قلت: وفي المعراج روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام حلق رأسه من يمين الحالق وعن الشافعي من يمين المحلوق فاعتبرنا يمين الحالق وهو يمين المحلوق . قال الكرماني : ذكره بعض أصحابنا ولم يعزه إلى أحد بل الأولى اتباع السنة فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بدأ بيمينه في الصحيح، وقد أخذ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقول الحجام حين قال ادن الشق الأيمن من رأسك وفيه حكاية معروفة | هـ. وهذا أيضاً يؤيد ما استصوبه في الفتح ويفيد أن خلافه ليس مما ثبت عند أهل المذهب قوله : ( وينبغي أن يحكم بضعف ما في الفتاوى) قال في الشرنبلالية أقول : لم يقتصر قاضيخان على ما نقله عنه في البحر لأنه نص على ما يوافق الهداية الرمي قبل الحلق يحل له كل شيء إلا الطيب والنساء، وعن أبي يوسف يحل له الطيب شيء غير النساء ثم إلى مكة يوم النحر أو غداً أو بعده فطف للركن سبعة أشواط بلا لأنه أبيح له التحلل فيقع به التحلل ا هـ. فلو كان التحلل بالرمي حاصلاً في غير الطيب والنساء لم يلزمه دم بتقليم الأظفار وتخريجه على قول الطحاوي عندهما بعيد كما لا يخفى.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: It is recommended (mustahab) and the requirement of the text is to begin with the right side of the head because of what is in the Two Sahihs that he (peace be upon him) said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to the right side, then the left, then he began to give it to the people. And in Fath al-Qadir: That is the correct view, and it contradicts what is mentioned in the madhhab. It is recommended to bury his hair, to make supplication at the time of shaving and after finishing with takbir, and if he throws the hair there is no harm, and it is disliked to throw it in a lavatory or washroom. Thus in Fatawa al-Alami. He may cut his nails and mustache after shaving following the sunna, and he should not take anything from his beard because it is mutilation, and if he does nothing is required of him. His statement: (And what is other than women is permissible for you), meaning by shaving, so perfume is permissible because of the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) in the Two Sahihs: she said, 'I perfumed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he entered ihram and when he exited ihram before he circumambulated the House.' And the motives such as intercourse are forbidden. It indicates that before shaving there is no permission for anything that was forbidden by ihram, and this is supported by what is in al-Mabsut. The conclusion is that in Hajj there are two tahalluls: one by shaving and the second by tawaf. And what is in al-Hidayah and others that ramy is not one of the causes of tahallul with us is contradicted by what is in Fatawa Qadikhan, and his wording: 'After ramy before shaving, everything is permissible for him except perfume and women.' And from Abu Yusuf: perfume is also permissible for him, even though women are not permissible. The correct is what we said, because perfume motivates intercourse, and we have only known the permissibility of perfume after shaving before Tawaf al-Ziyadah by tradition (athar). It is necessary to judge the weakness of what is in the Fatawa due to what we presented and due to what is in al-Muhit: 'If tahallul were permitted to him, then he washed his head with khitmi and trimmed his nail before shaving, a blood (dam) is due because ihram remains as it is only removed by shaving, so he has violated it.' And al-Tahawi mentioned that there is no dam upon him according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. That [blood] is the priority, so there is no contradiction in sufficiency because a quarter is like the whole as in shaving. His statement: (And in Fath al-Qadir the correct view) said in al-Nahr: It is supported by what is in al-Multaqat from the Imam: 'I shaved my head in Makkah, and the barber made mistakes in three things: when I sat down, he said face the qibla; I handed him the left side, he said start with the right; when I wanted to go, he said bury your hair, so I returned and buried it.' I said: And in al-Mi'raj it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved his head from the right side of the barber, and from al-Shafi'i from the right side of the shaved person, so we consider the right of the barber which is the right of the shaved person. Al-Kirmani said: Some of our companions mentioned it and did not attribute it to anyone, but the first is to follow the sunna, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) began with his right in the Sahih, and Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) took the saying of the cupper when he said: 'Bring the right side of your head near,' and there is a well-known story. This also supports what was deemed correct in al-Fath and indicates that its disagreement is not established among the people of the madhhab. His statement: (And it is necessary to judge the weakness of what is in the Fatawa) said in al-Sharnabaliyya: I say: Qadikhan did not limit himself to what was transmitted from him in al-Bahr, because he also stated what agrees with al-Hidayah before this with his saying: 'And exiting ihram is only by shaving or trimming, so if he shaves or trims, everything is permissible for him except women as long as he has not circumambulated the House'; that is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) from the Prophet (may peace be upon him). And after ramy before shaving, everything is permissible for him except perfume and women. And from Abu Yusuf, perfume is permissible for him. Something other than women, then to Makkah on the Day of Nahr or the next day or after it, and circumambulate the pillar seven circuits without [saying] because tahallul was permitted for him, so tahallul occurs by it. If tahallul by ramy had occurred in other than perfume and women, then trimming nails would not necessitate a dam, and its derivation based on the saying of al-Tahawi with them is far-fetched, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering the rulings related to shaving the head (halq) during Hajj and the associated legal dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding when perfume (tayyib) becomes permissible for the muhrim. The passage first addresses the recommended (mustahab) practice of beginning the shave from the right side of the head, citing the hadith in the Sahihayn where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed the barber to start with the right side. It then discusses other sunan: burying the hair, making dua and takbir, and the prohibition against cutting the beard. The core legal issue is the timing of tahallul (partial release from ihram). According to the Hanafi school, there are two tahalluls: the first occurs by shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir), which permits everything except women (i.e., sexual relations). The second occurs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which permits women. The text refutes the view found in Fatawa Qadikhan that after ramy (stoning) before halq, everything except perfume and women is permissible. It also reports Abu Yusuf's view that perfume becomes permissible after ramy. The correct Hanafi position, affirmed by the author, is that perfume is only permissible after halq, not after ramy, based on the hadith of Aisha that she perfumed the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he exited ihram before Tawaf, and the principle that perfume is a motivator for intercourse (dā'ī ilā al-jimā‘). The passage also includes a discussion of the beginning side of shaving, with a story from al-Multaqat and a reference to the Fath al-Qadir, concluding that starting with the right is the sunna. Finally, it addresses the issue of whether a dam (blood sacrifice) is required if one washes or trims nails before halq, and cites al-Tahawi's view that there is no dam according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but the preferred position is that a dam is due because ihram remains. The commentary ends by judging the view in Fatawa Qadikhan as weak, citing a contradiction within Qadikhan's own statements.

Key Terms
التحلل (at-tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram, which occurs in two stages: first by halq (permitting everything except women), second by Tawaf al-Ziyarah (permitting women).
الجناية (al-jinaayah): A violation committed during ihram that requires compensation (dam or sadaqah). Using perfume before halq is a jinaayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, when does perfume become permissible for a muhrim after the Day of Arafah?
A) After ramy only
B) After halq only
C) After both ramy and halq
D) Only after Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Key Takeaway
Perfume becomes halal only after shaving (halq), not after stoning (ramy), and using it earlier is a violation requiring a dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Pillar, Obligations, and Timing
Details legal ruling with conditions and a death exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah, distinguish its rukn (four circuits) from its wajibat, and apply the conditions for its validity and the compensation rules.

Core Idea
Four circuits are the pillar; three are wajib—missing a rukn invalidates, missing a wajib requires a dam.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah, is a central pillar of Hajj. This lesson unpacks its precise legal structure in the Hanafi school: which parts are essential (rukn), which are obligatory but compensable (wajib), and what conditions must be met for the act to be valid. We also examine the special case when a pilgrim dies after wuquf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
Recognize that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the second pillar of Hajj, performed after returning from Mina on the Day of Nahr or subsequent days.
Also called Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Rukn.
2
Distinguish between rukn and wajib
Note that the rukn is the greater part: four circuits. The remaining three circuits are wajib, meaning they are obligatory but if omitted unintentionally, a dam (blood sacrifice) compensates.
This is the correct Hanafi view (as-sahih). The Shafi'i school considers all seven circuits as rukn.
3
List the conditions (shurut) and wajibat
Conditions include Islam, ihram, wuquf, intention, performing most circuits (four), time within days of Nahr, place around Kaaba, and performing oneself (except if unconscious). Wajibat include walking, starting from Black Stone, completing seven circuits, purification, covering awrah, and performing within days of Nahr.
The order between ramy, halq, and tawaf is sunnah, not wajib.
4
Understand the time constraints
The earliest valid time is dawn of the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah). According to Abu Hanifa, the wajib time is one of the three days of Nahr. Delaying beyond that while able requires a dam. The rukn (four circuits) can be performed at any time in life if missed.
The best day is the first (Day of Nahr), like the sacrifice.
5
Apply the death-after-wuquf scenario
If a pilgrim dies after wuquf at Arafah and bequeaths that the Hajj be completed, a badanah (camel) is slaughtered for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and the remaining acts, and the Hajj is valid. This is based on the principle 'Hajj is Arafah' and the compensation rule.
This does not contradict the general rule that Tawaf al-Ziyarah cannot be substituted except in this case.

البيت من مني ا هـ. هذا وشرائط صحته : الإسلام وتقديم الإحرام والوقوف والنية وإتيان أكثره والزمان هو يوم النحر وبعده، والمكان وهو حول البيت داخل المسجد، وكونه بنفسه ولو محمولاً فلا تجوز النيابة إلا لمغمى عليه . وواجباته المشي للقادر والتيامن وإتمام السبعة والطهارة عن الحدث وستر العورة وفعله في أيام النحر، وأما الترتيب بينه وبين الرمي والحلق فسنة ولا مفسد للطواف ولا فوات قبل الممات ولا يجزئ عنه البدل إلا إذا مات بعد الوقوف بعرفة وأوصى بإتمام الحج تجب البدنة لطواف الزيارة وجاز حجه ا هـ (لباب). أي صح وكمل لكن في مناسك الطرابلسي عن محمد فيمن مات بعد وقوفه بعرفة وأوصى بإتمام الحج يذبح عنه بدنة الطواف ويؤيده ما في قاضيخان والسراجية أن الحاج عن الميت إذا مات بعد الوقوف بعرفة جاز عن الميت لأنه أدى ركن الحج أي ركنه الأعظم الذي لا يفوت إلا بفوته لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «الحج عرفة» وهو لا ينافي في ما سبق من وجوب البدنة فإنه يجب من مال الميت حينئذ ا هـ. شارح لباب قوله : (وقد ورد في الحديث الخ ) قال في اللباب : وإذا فرغ من الطواف رجع إلى
His statement: (Then to Makkah on the Day of Nahr or the next day or after it, and circumambulate the pillar seven circuits without raml and sa'ee, if you have performed them earlier, otherwise do them later) meaning then go on one of these three days to perform the second pillar of the two pillars of Hajj, and we have already stated that the pillar is the greater part of it, which is four circuits according to the correct view, and what is beyond that is wajib and is compensated for by blood. And the earliest time for its validity is when the dawn of the Day of Nahr breaks, even if before ramy and halq, and there is no other time after which its validity is lost, rather its time is for life. As for the wajib, it is to perform it on one of the three days according to Abu Hanifa, such that if he delays it beyond them while able, a dam is required, and the best of them is the first, like the sacrifice. And it is established in the hadith that he (peace be upon him) circumambulated after the noon prayer on the Day of Nahr for the pillar, and it indicates that he is free to choose between performing raml and sa'ee if he circumambulates. And the correct is what we said, because perfume is a motive for intercourse, and we have only known the permissibility of perfume after halq before Tawaf al-Ziyarah by tradition. So it is better to refer his latter statement to his first statement because it is more binding in agreeing with what is in al-Hidayah, and its evidence is in the Two Sahihs, and because the first contradicts the second. And his statement 'And we have only known the permissibility of perfume...' is an answer to an implied question, as if someone said: perfume is a motive for women, so it is absolutely prohibited, so he specified it to be permitted by ramy and made halal by halq due to tradition, but he did not bring evidence for the permissibility by ramy of anything, so the reference is to his first statement agreeing with al-Hidayah and his limiting of tahallul to halq by his saying 'exiting ihram is only by halq.' And thereby it is known the invalidity of what is attributed to Qadikhan that halq does not permit perfume. The author's statement: (circumambulate the pillar seven circuits). Al-Ramli said: It is called Tawaf al-Ziyarah, Tawaf al-Ifadah, Tawaf of the Day of Nahr, and Tawaf al-Rukn as in al-'Ayni, and it will come that Tawaf al-Sadr is called Tawaf al-Ifadah because for its sake one pours forth from Mina to the House. These are the conditions of its validity: Islam, preceding ihram, standing at Arafah, intention, performing most of it, and its time is the Day of Nahr and after it, and its place is around the House inside the Masjid, and it must be performed by oneself even if carried, so proxy is not allowed except for one who is unconscious. Its wajibat are: walking for the able, right tayammun (starting each circuit from the Black Stone), completing all seven, purification from major impurity, covering the awrah, and performing it within the days of Nahr. As for the order between it and ramy and halq, it is sunnah and does not invalidate the tawaf, nor does it become impossible before death, and no substitute suffices for it except if one dies after standing at Arafah and bequeathed to complete the Hajj, then a badanah (camel) becomes obligatory for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and his Hajj is valid. That is from Lubab. Meaning it is valid and complete, but in Manasik al-Tarabulsuli from Muhammad: if someone dies after standing at Arafah and bequeathed to complete the Hajj, a badanah is slaughtered for him for Muzdalifah, ramy, al-Ziyarah, and al-Sadr, and his Hajj is valid. This is evidence that if he dies at Arafah after the reality of wuquf, the badanah compensates for the remaining acts, and it does not contradict what is in al-Mabsut that a badanah is obligatory for Tawaf al-Ziyarah if the remaining acts are performed except the tawaf. And it is supported by what is in Qadikhan and al-Sirajiyya that the Hajj for the deceased, if he dies after standing at Arafah, is valid because he performed the pillar of Hajj, i.e., its greatest pillar which is only lost by its loss, due to his (peace be upon him) saying 'Hajj is Arafah', and it does not contradict the foregoing obligation of a badanah, for it is due from the wealth of the deceased then. Commentator of Lubab said: (And it is established in the hadith...) He said in al-Lubab: And when he finishes the tawaf, he returns to...
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq focuses on the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Rukn), which is the second pillar of Hajj. The commentary explains the timing: it begins at dawn of the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) and can be performed on that day or the following two days (the three days of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa). It distinguishes between the rukn (pillar) and the wajib (obligatory) components: the rukn is four circuits (ashwat) according to the correct view, while the remaining three circuits are wajib, meaning they are required but can be compensated with a dam (blood sacrifice) if omitted unintentionally. The passage also lists the conditions (shurut) and wajibat of the tawaf. Conditions include Islam, being in a state of ihram, having performed wuquf at Arafah, intention, performing most of the circuits, time (day of Nahr and after), place (around the Kaaba inside the Masjid), and performing it oneself unless unconscious. Wajibat include walking (if able), starting each circuit from the Black Stone (tayamun), completing all seven circuits, being in a state of purity (tahara) from major impurity (hadath), covering the awrah, and performing it within the days of Nahr. The order between ramy, halq, and tawaf is sunnah, not wajib, so if done out of order it does not invalidate the tawaf. A special ruling is given for someone who dies after wuquf at Arafah but before completing tawaf: if the deceased bequeathed to complete the Hajj, a badanah (camel) is slaughtered on his behalf for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and the Hajj is valid. This is based on the principle that the pillar of Hajj is wuquf at Arafah ('Hajj is Arafah'), and the remaining acts can be compensated for. The text also returns to the previous dispute about perfume, repeating the point that the correct view is that perfume is halal after halq before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and that this is established by tradition. Finally, it criticizes the attribution to Qadikhan that halq does not permit perfume, concluding that such a view is invalid.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after returning from Mina on the Day of Nahr or the following days; it is the second pillar of Hajj.
الركن (ar-rukun): The essential component of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which is four circuits according to the correct Hanafi view.
الواجب (al-wajib): The obligatory components of Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the rukn, including the remaining three circuits and other conditions like purification, covering awrah, etc.
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel (or other large animal) slaughtered as a blood sacrifice (dam) to compensate for omitted wajibat or as a penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of circuits that constitute the rukn (pillar) of Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) All seven circuits
B) Four circuits
C) Three circuits
D) One circuit

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a pillar of Hajj with four circuits as its rukn and the remaining three as wajib; missing a wajib requires a dam, but missing the rukn invalidates the tawaf.

Rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (Tawaf al-Ifadah)
Commentary on the time, obligations, and conditions of Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and obligations of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify the correct time for its wajib performance according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The rukn of tawaf is four circuits; performing it within three days is wajib; only halq lifts the ban on women.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a central pillar of Hajj. This commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies its time, components, and effects – including the crucial distinction that tawaf alone does not permit marital relations until shaving is done. Understanding these details ensures the pilgrim fulfills the rites correctly and avoids unnecessary penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification of Tawaf al-Ziyarah: its core (four circuits) is rukn (pillar); completing all seven circuits and performing within the three days of al-Nahr is wajib (obligatory).
The passage explicitly states: 'the pillar is most of it, which is four circuits on the correct view, and what is extra is wajib.'
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Tawaf al-Ifadah after Dhuhr on the Day of Sacrifice. This indicates the earliest permissible time.
The dalil is a hadith from the Sahihayn; it is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's action shows the time starts after sunrise on the Day of Sacrifice, but does not set a deadline; the three-day limit is derived from other evidence (juristic reasoning).
The text also uses 'Akhbaar' (reports) to determine the permissibility of perfume after halq before tawaf.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Observe the disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds the wajib time is the three days of al-Nahr (10th–12th Dhul Hijjah); others (e.g., some later scholars) allow Tawaf al-Ifadah anytime during the days of Tashriq. The Hanafi position ties the wajib to these three days; delay beyond them with ability incurs a dam.
The commentator sides with Abu Hanifa and Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the wajib performance is within the three days; if delayed, a dam is required. The best day is the first (Day of Sacrifice).
The text also discusses a menstruating woman: if she becomes pure on the last day and can perform four circuits before sunset, she must do so; otherwise, no penalty.

His statement: (Then to Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice or the next day or after it, and perform for the pillar seven circuits without ramal and perform sa'y if you have advanced them before, otherwise do [them] now.) That is, then go on one of these three days to perform the second pillar of the two pillars of Hajj. We have already stated that the pillar is most of it, which is four circuits according to the correct view, and what is extra is wajib compensated by a dam. The earliest time of validity is when dawn breaks on the Day of Sacrifice, even before stoning and shaving, and there is no other time the validity of which is lost by its passing; rather its time is the whole of one's lifetime. As for the wajib, it is to perform it on one of the three days according to Abu Hanifa, such that if he delays it beyond them with ability, a dam is incumbent. The best of them is the first, like the sacrificial animal. It has been reported in the hadith that he (peace be upon him) performed tawaf after Dhuhr prayer on the Day of Sacrifice for the pillar, and it indicates that he is given a choice in advancing ramal and sa'y if he performs tawaf...
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). The commentator explains that the pilgrim should proceed to Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) or the following two days to perform seven circuits (ashwat) for the pillar of Hajj. He clarifies that the essential pillar (rukn) of tawaf is four circuits according to the correct view in the Hanafi school; additional circuits are wajib (obligatory) and if omitted can be compensated by a dam (sacrifice). The earliest valid time for this tawaf is at dawn on the Day of Sacrifice, even if stoning (ramy) and shaving (halq) have not yet been done. However, the time for the wajib performance is the three days of al-Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) according to Imam Abu Hanifa; if delayed beyond this period with ability, a dam becomes due. The best time is the first day (10th), analogous to the sacrifice (udhiya). The hadith is cited that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed this tawaf after Dhuhr on the Day of Sacrifice, indicating flexibility in whether ramal and sa'y are done before or after. The commentator then discusses the issue of khiyar (choice) in performing ramal and sa'y, and the relationship between halq (shaving) and tawaf for the permissibility of women (i.e., conjugal relations). The correct position is that the tawaf does not halt the restriction on women; only halq does, as shaving completes the state of ihram exit. The commentary refutes a report attributed to Qadikhan that halq does not permit perfume, affirming that halq is the key to exiting ihram. It then lists the conditions for the validity of tawaf: Islam, prior ihram, standing at Arafat, intention, performing most of the circuits, time (Day of Sacrifice and after), place (around the Kaaba inside the mosque), performing it oneself (even if carried, but agency not allowed except for the unconscious). Obligations of tawaf include walking for the able, making tayammun (touching the Black Stone with the right hand), completing seven circuits, ritual purity, covering the aurah, and performing it within the days of al-Nahr. The order between tawaf, ramy, and halq is sunnah. The tawaf is not invalidated by anything except pre-death omission; it cannot be substituted except if the pilgrim dies after Arafat and willed completion of Hajj, then a badanah (camel) is due for Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The passage also discusses the case of a menstruating woman who becomes pure at the end of the days of al-Nahr: if she can perform four circuits before sunset and fails, she owes a dam; if she cannot, nothing is due. The lesson concludes by emphasizing that the prohibition of women (muharramat) is lifted only after shaving, not after tawaf, and that delaying tawaf beyond its days is makruh tahrimi (disliked to prohibition) due to leaving the wajib.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca during Hajj after returning from Mina; also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
التحلل (al-tahallul): The state of exiting ihram, achieved primarily by shaving (halq) and permitting formerly prohibited actions.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component of an act; here, the pillar of tawaf is four circuits, without which the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Seven circuits
B) Four circuits
C) Three circuits
D) One circuit

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah's pillar is four circuits; performing all seven within the three days of al-Nahr is wajib; only shaving, not tawaf, permits marital relations.
