Raml, Sa'i, and Halq: Their Roles in Hajj
Commentary on raml, sa'i, and halq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the timing of raml and sa'i and explain why halq is the act that releases one from ihram, not tawaf.

Core Idea
Halq releases you from ihram, not tawaf; raml and sa'i are performed with tawaf al-qudum if possible, otherwise with tawaf al-ifada.

In this passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the commentator clarifies the roles of raml, sa'i, and halq in Hajj. Understanding when to perform raml and sa'i—whether with the arrival tawaf or the obligatory tawaf—and recognizing that halq is the decisive act of exiting ihram are essential for a valid Hajj without penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify timing of raml and sa'i
If you perform raml and sa'i earlier (with tawaf al-qudum), they are fulfilled; otherwise, they must be performed later (with tawaf al-ifada). They are not repeated in Hajj.
The preferred practice is to delay them to the obligatory tawaf so they follow the compulsory act.
2
Understand the release from ihram
Halq (shaving the head) is what makes women permissible, not tawaf. The commentator emphasizes that shaving is the sole act of release (muhallil).
This refutes the common misconception that tawaf alone suffices.
3
Analyze the proof
The author uses an analogy to revocable divorce: just as divorce takes full effect only after the waiting period ends, halq becomes effective only after tawaf is performed.
Evidence: if a pilgrim performs tawaf but does not shave, nothing becomes permissible until he shaves.
4
Apply the implications
If one intentionally omits halq and instead trims a nail or covers the head intending to exit ihram, that is a violation requiring a penalty (dam).
The permissibility of women is suspended upon completing the four circuits of tawaf, but actually released by halq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج باب الإحرام
7.4
رمل وسعى إن قدمتهما وإلا فعلا وحل لك النساء وكره تأخيره عن أيام النحر ثم إلى النساء إلى للقدوم وفي تأخيرهما لطواف الركن وأنهما لا يتكرران في الحج ، ولم يتكلم على الأفضلية وقالوا : الأفضل تأخير هما لطواف الركن ليصيرا تبعاً للفرض دون السنة قوله : (وحل لك النساء) يعني بالحلق السابق لا بالطواف لأن الحلق هو المحلل دون الطواف غير أنه آخر عمله في حق ا ما بعد الطواف، فإذا طاف عمل الحلق عمله كالطلاق الرجعي آخر عمله إلى انقضاء العدة لحاجته إلى الاسترداد فإذا انقضت عمل الطلاق عمله فبانت به والدليل على ذلك أنه لو لم يحلق حتى طاف بالبيت لم يحل له شيء حتى يحلق . كذا ذكر الشارح وغيره، وهكذا صرح في فتح القدير أنه لا يخرج من الإحرام إلا بالحلق فأفاد أنه لو ترك الحلق أصلاً وقلم ظفره أو غطى رأسه قاصداً التحلل من الإحرام كان ذلك جناية موجبة للجزاء وحل النساء موقوف على الركن منها وهي أربعة فقط قوله : (وكره تأخيره عن أيام النحر ) أي تأخير الطواف كراهة تحريم لترك الواجب وهو فيها، وأشار به إلى رد ما ذكره القدوري في شرحه من أن آخره آخر أيام التشريق، ولو قال «وكره تأخيرهما عن أيام النحر لكان أولى ليفيد حكم الحلق كالطواف ومحل الكراهة ولزوم الدم بالتأخير إنما هو عند الإمكان كما في المحيط من أن الحائض إذا طهرت في آخر أيام النحر فإن أمكنها الطواف قبل الغروب ولم تفعل فعليها دم للتأخير، وإن لم يمكنها طواف أربعة أشواط فلا شيء عليها، ولو حاضت بعد ما قدرت على الطواف فلم تطف حتى مضى الوقت لزمها الدم لأنها مقصرة بتفريطها، وفي الظهيرية وليالي أيام النحر منها .
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. 7.4 Raml and sa'i: if you perform them earlier [with tawaf al-qudum] then done; otherwise, they are performed [later], and women become permissible to you, and it is disliked to delay it beyond the days of nahr. Then to women to [for] al-qudum, and regarding delaying them for the rukn tawaf, and that they are not repeated in Hajj. He did not discuss the preference, and they said: the preference is to delay them for the tawaf al-rukn to make them follow the obligatory [tawaf] rather than the sunnah. His statement: (and women become permissible to you) means by the previous shaving, not by tawaf, because shaving is the permissible agent, not tawaf, except that it is his last action in relation to what is after tawaf. So when he performs tawaf, the action of shaving takes effect like revocable divorce: its last action is until the expiration of the waiting period due to the need for revocation; when the waiting period expires, the divorce takes effect and she becomes separated. The evidence for that is that if he did not shave until he made tawaf of the House, nothing becomes permissible to him until he shaves. Thus mentioned the commentator and others, and similarly it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that one does not exit ihram except by shaving. So it conveys that if he did not shave at all and trimmed his nail or covered his head intending to exit ihram, that is a violation requiring a penalty, and the permissibility of women is suspended upon the rukn of it, which are only four [circuits]. His statement: (and it is disliked to delay it beyond the days of nahr) i.e., delaying tawaf with dislike of prohibition due to leaving an obligation which is in them. And he indicated by this a refutation of what al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that its end is the end of the days of tashriq. If he had said 'and it is disliked to delay them beyond the days of nahr' it would have been better to convey the ruling of shaling like tawaf. The place of dislike and requirement of blood for delay is only when possible, as in al-Muhit: if a menstruating woman becomes pure at the end of the days of nahr and she can perform tawaf before sunset but does not do so, she must give blood for delay; if she cannot perform four circuits, then nothing is upon her. If she menstruated after she was able to perform tawaf and did not perform until the time passed, blood becomes obligatory because she was negligent. In al-Zahiriyya: the nights of the days of nahr are included.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It covers several rulings. First, regarding raml (quick walking) and sa'i (running) in Hajj: if one performs them with the tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), then they are done; otherwise they must be performed later, typically with the tawaf al-ifada (the obligatory tawaf). They are not repeated in Hajj. The preferred practice is to delay them to the tawaf al-rukn so they follow the obligatory act. Second, the permissibility of women (i.e., sexual relations) after ihram occurs by shaving (halq) the head, not by tawaf. The author draws an analogy: just as a revocable divorce only becomes fully effective after the waiting period (iddah) ends, similarly tawaf alone does not release one; shaving is the actual release. Evidence: if one does not shave even after tawaf, nothing becomes halal until shaving. If one deliberately omits shaving and instead trims a nail or covers the head intending to exit ihram, that is a violation requiring a penalty (dam). The permissibility of women is suspended upon completing the four circuits of tawaf. Third, delaying tawaf beyond the days of nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah) is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it involves leaving a wajib. This ruling applies only when one is able to perform tawaf in time. For example, if a menstruating woman becomes pure on the last day of nahr and can perform tawaf before sunset but delays, she must offer a dam. If she cannot perform four circuits, no penalty is required. If she becomes able but delays out of negligence, a dam becomes due. The nights of the days of nahr are included in the time.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Quick walking with small steps in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum, specific to men.
سعي (sa'i): Running or walking between Safa and Marwah seven times, an obligatory ritual of Hajj and Umrah.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, the act that releases one from ihram for men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What releases a pilgrim from ihram in the Hanafi school?
A) Tawaf al-ifada
B) Sa'i
C) Halq or taqsir
D) Ramy al-Jamarat

Key Takeaway
Halq is the essential act of exiting ihram, and it becomes effective only after tawaf al-ifada.

The Timing of Tawaf and the Penalty for Delay
Commentary on delaying tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying tawaf beyond the days of nahr and identify when a dam is required based on ability.

Core Idea
Delaying tawaf beyond the days of nahr is prohibitively disliked and may require a dam if one was able to perform it earlier.

This part of the commentary addresses the timing of tawaf al-ifada. Delaying it beyond the appointed days is considered makruh tahrimi, and the penalty of a dam applies only when the pilgrim was capable of performing tawaf in time but delayed out of negligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on delay
The author says it is disliked to delay tawaf beyond the days of nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah). This is a karaha tahrimiya because it involves leaving a wajib (the defined time).
The passage refutes al-Quduri's view that the time extends to the end of tashriq days.
2
Understand the condition for penalty
A dam (penalty) is due only if the person was able to perform tawaf within the days of nahr but delayed.
If too weak or unable, no penalty.
3
Apply to the menstruating woman case
If a woman becomes pure on the last day of nahr and can perform tawaf before sunset, she must do so; otherwise a dam is due.
If she cannot perform four circuits, no penalty. Negligence after being able triggers dam.
4
Note the inclusion of nights
The nights of the days of nahr are also considered part of the time.
So the time includes the nights between 10th to 13th.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج باب الإحرام
7.4
رمل وسعى إن قدمتهما وإلا فعلا وحل لك النساء وكره تأخيره عن أيام النحر ثم إلى النساء إلى للقدوم وفي تأخيرهما لطواف الركن وأنهما لا يتكرران في الحج ، ولم يتكلم على الأفضلية وقالوا : الأفضل تأخير هما لطواف الركن ليصيرا تبعاً للفرض دون السنة قوله : (وحل لك النساء) يعني بالحلق السابق لا بالطواف لأن الحلق هو المحلل دون الطواف غير أنه آخر عمله في حق ا ما بعد الطواف، فإذا طاف عمل الحلق عمله كالطلاق الرجعي آخر عمله إلى انقضاء العدة لحاجته إلى الاسترداد فإذا انقضت عمل الطلاق عمله فبانت به والدليل على ذلك أنه لو لم يحلق حتى طاف بالبيت لم يحل له شيء حتى يحلق . كذا ذكر الشارح وغيره، وهكذا صرح في فتح القدير أنه لا يخرج من الإحرام إلا بالحلق فأفاد أنه لو ترك الحلق أصلاً وقلم ظفره أو غطى رأسه قاصداً التحلل من الإحرام كان ذلك جناية موجبة للجزاء وحل النساء موقوف على الركن منها وهي أربعة فقط قوله : (وكره تأخيره عن أيام النحر ) أي تأخير الطواف كراهة تحريم لترك الواجب وهو فيها، وأشار به إلى رد ما ذكره القدوري في شرحه من أن آخره آخر أيام التشريق، ولو قال «وكره تأخيرهما عن أيام النحر لكان أولى ليفيد حكم الحلق كالطواف ومحل الكراهة ولزوم الدم بالتأخير إنما هو عند الإمكان كما في المحيط من أن الحائض إذا طهرت في آخر أيام النحر فإن أمكنها الطواف قبل الغروب ولم تفعل فعليها دم للتأخير، وإن لم يمكنها طواف أربعة أشواط فلا شيء عليها، ولو حاضت بعد ما قدرت على الطواف فلم تطف حتى مضى الوقت لزمها الدم لأنها مقصرة بتفريطها، وفي الظهيرية وليالي أيام النحر منها .
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. 7.4 Raml and sa'i: if you perform them earlier [with tawaf al-qudum] then done; otherwise, they are performed [later], and women become permissible to you, and it is disliked to delay it beyond the days of nahr. Then to women to [for] al-qudum, and regarding delaying them for the rukn tawaf, and that they are not repeated in Hajj. He did not discuss the preference, and they said: the preference is to delay them for the tawaf al-rukn to make them follow the obligatory [tawaf] rather than the sunnah. His statement: (and women become permissible to you) means by the previous shaving, not by tawaf, because shaving is the permissible agent, not tawaf, except that it is his last action in relation to what is after tawaf. So when he performs tawaf, the action of shaving takes effect like revocable divorce: its last action is until the expiration of the waiting period due to the need for revocation; when the waiting period expires, the divorce takes effect and she becomes separated. The evidence for that is that if he did not shave until he made tawaf of the House, nothing becomes permissible to him until he shaves. Thus mentioned the commentator and others, and similarly it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that one does not exit ihram except by shaving. So it conveys that if he did not shave at all and trimmed his nail or covered his head intending to exit ihram, that is a violation requiring a penalty, and the permissibility of women is suspended upon the rukn of it, which are only four [circuits]. His statement: (and it is disliked to delay it beyond the days of nahr) i.e., delaying tawaf with dislike of prohibition due to leaving an obligation which is in them. And he indicated by this a refutation of what al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that its end is the end of the days of tashriq. If he had said 'and it is disliked to delay them beyond the days of nahr' it would have been better to convey the ruling of shaling like tawaf. The place of dislike and requirement of blood for delay is only when possible, as in al-Muhit: if a menstruating woman becomes pure at the end of the days of nahr and she can perform tawaf before sunset but does not do so, she must give blood for delay; if she cannot perform four circuits, then nothing is upon her. If she menstruated after she was able to perform tawaf and did not perform until the time passed, blood becomes obligatory because she was negligent. In al-Zahiriyya: the nights of the days of nahr are included.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
دم (dam): A penalty offering of an animal sacrifice for missing a wajib of Hajj.

Timing of Stoning on the Second and Third Days of Tashriq
Ruling on valid and disliked times for stoning on the second and third days of Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid and disliked times for stoning on the second and third days of Tashriq according to the Hanafi school and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the end time.

Core Idea
Valid stoning time: zawal to fajr (or sunrise); disliked after sunset but still valid.

The ritual of stoning the jamarat is a wajib act of Hajj with specific timing. On the second and third days of Tashriq, the beginning time is clear: after zawal. However, the end time is subject to a well-known difference within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it ends at fajr, while his two disciples say sunrise. The commentator navigates these views, clarifying the operative ruling for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that stoning (rami al-jimar) on the days of Tashriq is a wajib act of Hajj; missing it requires a dam (penalty).
The passage focuses on timing, not the obligation itself.
2
State the beginning time
The matn specifies 'after zawal' (after noon). This is the agreed start time for the second and third days.
Stoning before zawal is invalid.
3
Distinguish between valid and disliked times
The commentary extracts two times: a time of validity (zawal to sunrise) and a time of dislike (after sunset to sunrise). Stoning at night is valid but disliked.
This is unlike the first day, which has four times.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the valid time ends at fajr; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it extends to sunrise. The author leans towards fajr as the end of performance time, citing al-Bada'i and al-Murshidi.
The difference affects whether stoning after fajr is within the performance time or becomes qada.
5
Determine the consequence of delay
If stoning is delayed beyond its designated day, qada and a dam are required. The time for qada extends until sunset of the fourth day of Tashriq.
After that, the obligation is dropped.

Then to Mina, and stone the three jamarat on the second of nahr after zawal, starting with the one nearest the mosque, then the one next to it, then Jamrat al-Aqaba, and pause at each stoning after stoning, then likewise the next day, then likewise thereafter if you stay (if you stay). That is, then travel to Mina and stone the jamarat following the example of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. He did not mention staying overnight in Mina because it is not obligatory since the purpose is stoning, but it is sunnah, as al-Asbijabi said: He should not stay overnight in Mecca nor on the road, and it is disliked to stay overnight other than in Mina during the days of Mina. And he indicated by his statement 'after zawal' to its beginning time on the second and third, such that if one stoned before zawal it is not valid, and he did not mention its end, which extends until sunrise, valid and disliked. Thus in al-Muhit. So it appears that it has two times: a time of validity and a time of dislike, unlike stoning on the first day which has four times as we explained. And what is in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that the second day of Tashriq is like the first, and if one intends to depart on that day he may stone before zawal, but it is not permissible before zawal for one who does not intend to depart, is contrary to the apparent narration, for the apparent narration is that its time does not enter in the two days except after zawal absolutely. In al-Muhit: If he delays all stoning to the fourth day, he stones them in order because all days of Tashriq are times for stoning, so he makes them up in order like the original sunnah, and upon him is one dam according to Abu Hanifa because the violations are of one type so one expiation suffices. If he leaves them until the sun sets on the last days of Tashriq, they are waived... the discussion of that is in the chapter on i'tikaf. His statement: (and it extends to sunrise of the next day) is mentioned similarly in al-Bahr al-Umariq, Mansak al-Farsi, and al-Tarabulusi. But it contradicts what is in Lubab al-Manasik and its commentary that when fajr rises, the time for performance has passed according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] contrary to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and the time for qada remains by agreement. So it is explicit that the end of stoning in these two days is fajr, and the commentator al-Murshidi affirmed it, and similar in Mansak al-Aziz. Evidence for it is the statement of the author of al-Bada'i: if he delays stoning in them to the night and stoned before fajr, it is valid and nothing is upon him because night is a time of stoning in the days of stoning due to the hadith we narrated. And the statement of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: the disliked time on the first day is between fajr and sunrise, and likewise on the fourth day according to Abu Hanifa, and between all these days are the three nights. And the statement of al-Haddadi in al-Jawhara: if he stoned at night before fajr it is valid and nothing is upon him. It seems there is a difference in narration. Then in al-Mansak al-Awsat by Mulla Sinan al-Rumi, the disagreement is mentioned: he said our companions said that the time for performing stoning on the first and second days of Tashriq is from zawal to fajr of the next day, and some said until sunrise of the next day. Thus in Hashiyat al-Madani from Hashiyat his shaykh. His statement: (so it appears that it has two times, etc.): so the time of validity is from zawal to sunrise, and the time of dislike is from sunset to sunrise. And this is all the time of performance on the second and third days. In al-Lubab and its commentary: when fajr rises, i.e., the morning of the fourth day, the time of performance has passed according to Imam contrary to them, and the time of qada remains by agreement until the end of the days of Tashriq. So if he delays stoning from its time appointed for each day, he must perform qada and a penalty which is the requirement of blood, and the time for qada ends with sunset of the fourth day. He will indicate that shortly.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage expands on the timing of stoning (rami al-jimar) on the second and third days of Tashriq (11th and 12th Dhul Hijjah). The matn states 'after zawal' (after noon) as the start time. The commentary explains that the valid time for stoning on these days extends from zawal until sunrise of the next day. However, it is disliked (makruh) to stone after sunset until sunrise, although still valid. This contrasts with the first day (10th) which has four valid times. The passage notes a difference of narration: some sources say the valid time ends at fajr of the next day, while others say sunrise. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the author is that the end is fajr, based on the hadith that night is a time for stoning. If one delays all stoning to the fourth day (12th or 13th, depending), he must stone in order and offer one dam (penalty) according to Abu Hanifa. If stoning is not performed by sunset of the last day, it is waived. The passage then discusses that if one delays stoning on a specific day beyond its appointed time (i.e., after the valid window), he must perform qada (make-up) and the penalty of a dam. The qada time extends until the end of the days of Tashriq (sunset of the fourth day). Overall, this passage gives a detailed Hanafi ruling on the temporal boundaries of the stoning ritual.

Key Terms
رمي الجمار (rami al-jimar): The ritual of throwing pebbles at three pillars (jamarat) in Mina during Hajj.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith (noon).
أيام التشريق (ayam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th Dhul Hijjah).
وقت الكراهة (waqt al-karahah): The time during which an act is valid but disliked (makruh). In this context, stoning after sunset until sunrise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sunrise of the next day
B) Fajr of the next day
C) Sunset of the same day
D) Midnight

Key Takeaway
On the second and third days of Tashriq, stoning is valid from zawal to fajr, with a disliked period after sunset; the mufta bihi follows Imam Abu Hanifa's view that fajr is the performance boundary.

Timing of Rami on the Second and Third Days of Tashriq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time of ada for rami.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the end time of ada for rami on the second and third days of Tashriq and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Stoning after fajr on the third day is qada, not ada, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the precise timing for stoning the jamarat on the second and third days of Tashriq. While the beginning time is agreed upon (zawal), the end of the optimal performance time (ada) is disputed within the Hanafi school. Understanding this ikhtilaf and its practical consequence is essential for correct Hajj practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ramy al-jimar (stoning the three jamarat) on the second and third days of Tashriq. It is wajib in the Hanafi school.
The beginning time is zawal (sun past meridian); stoning before zawal is invalid.
2
State the two positions on the end of ada time
Imam Abu Hanifa: the time of ada ends at fajr (dawn) of the next day. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the time of ada ends at sunrise of the next day. After that time, the stoning becomes qada (makeup).
Both agree that the time of qada extends until sunset of the fourth day of Tashriq.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
Imam Abu Hanifa relies on a hadith that stoning at night before fajr is valid, implying that after fajr the time changes. The Sahibayn rely on the apparent practice of the Prophet (stoning after zawal) and analogy with the first day where sunrise is the end.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but referenced in al-Bada'i.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view (ada ends at fajr). The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): if one stones between fajr and sunrise on the third day, according to Imam it is qada (requiring dam), while according to the Sahibayn it is valid ada.
The later scholars (e.g., al-Lubab, al-Murshidi) affirm Imam's view.
5
Note the additional ruling on delaying all stoning
If one delays all rami to the fourth day, he must stone in order and pay one dam (according to Abu Hanifa). If he abandons it entirely until sunset of the fourth day, the stoning drops and one dam is due by consensus.
This shows the structure of qada and penalty.

Then proceed to Mina and stone the jamarat on the second day of sacrifice after zawal, beginning with what is nearest to the mosque, then what is next, then the Jamrat al-Aqaba. Stop at each stoning, then stone the next day similarly, and the day after similarly if you stay. Meaning: then go to Mina and stone the jamarat following the Prophet ﷺ. He did not mention staying overnight in Mina because it is not obligatory, as the purpose is stoning, but it is sunnah. Al-Asbijabi said: He does not stay overnight in Makkah nor on the road, and it is disliked to stay overnight outside the days of Mina. He indicated by 'after zawal' the beginning of its time on the second and third days, such that if one stones before zawal it is not valid. He did not mention its end—it extends to sunrise, valid but disliked. Thus it appears there are two times: a time of validity and a time of dislike, unlike the first day which has four times as we explained. What is in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that the second day of Tashriq is like the first day, and if one intends to depart early he may stone before zawal, and it is only invalid before zawal for one who does not intend to depart, is [interpreted] as contrary to the zahir al-riwaya, for the zahir al-riwaya is that the time does not enter on these two days except after zawal absolutely. In al-Muhit: If one delays all stoning to the fourth day, he stones them in order because all the days of Tashriq are a time for stoning, so he performs qada in order like the sunnah, and upon him is one dam according to Abu Hanifa because the violations (jinayat) are of one type, so one expiation applies. If he abandons them until the sun sets on the last day of Tashriq, the stoning drops due to the expiry of its time, and upon him is one dam by agreement. ... The stoning: regarding the word in the chapter of i'tikaf: his saying: (it extends to sunrise of the next day) is mentioned similarly in al-Bahr al-Amiq, and Manasik al-Farisi and al-Tarabulusi, but it contradicts what is in Lubab al-Manasik and its commentary that when fajr rises, the time of ada has passed according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and the time of qada remains by agreement. So it clearly states that the end of stoning on these two days is fajr. The commentator al-Murshidi affirmed it, and similar is in Manasik al-Afif. It is supported by the statement of the author of al-Bada'i: 'If he delays stoning on them to night and stones before fajr, it is valid and nothing is due upon him because the night is a time for stoning during the stoning days, due to the hadith we narrated.' And the statement of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'The disliked time on the first day is between fajr and sunrise, and likewise on the fourth day according to Abu Hanifa, and between all these days are the three nights.' And the statement of al-Hadadi in al-Jawhara: 'If he stones at night before fajr, it is valid and nothing is due.' There seems to be a difference of narration. Then I saw in al-Manasik al-Awsat by Mulla Sinan al-Rumi a narration of the ikhtilaf where he said: 'Our companions said that the time for performing the stoning on the first and second days of Tashriq is from zawal until fajr of the next day, and some said until sunrise of the next day.' This is from the marginalia of al-Madani from his shaykh. His saying: (then it appears it has two times) - the time of validity is from zawal to sunrise, and the time of dislike from sunset to sunrise. All of this is the time of ada on the second and third days. He said in al-Lubab and its commentary: 'When fajr rises, i.e., the morning of the fourth day, the time of ada expires according to Imam contrary to the two, and the time of qada remains by agreement until the end of the days of Tashriq. So if he delays the stoning from its appointed time each day, qada and compensation (dam) are incumbent, and the time of qada expires with sunset of the fourth day.' He will indicate this soon. Thus it becomes clear that stoning has a time of ada and a time of qada.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the timing of stoning the jamarat (ramy al-jimar) on the second and third days of Tashriq. The author begins by stating the prescribed sequence: stone the three jamarat after zawal (sun past the meridian), starting with the one nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then al-Aqaba. He notes that staying overnight in Mina is not wajib but sunnah. The core ruling is that the time for rami on these two days begins at zawal and extends to the next day's sunrise, with a disliked time from sunset to sunrise. However, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi disagreement about the end time: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the time of ada ends at fajr (dawn), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it extends until sunrise. The author cites numerous sources confirming this ikhtilaf. He also discusses the consequences of delaying rami: if all stoning is delayed to the fourth day, one must do it in order and pay one dam (according to Abu Hanifa). If one abandons it completely until sunset of the fourth day, the stoning is waived and one dam is due by consensus. The passage summarizes that rami has two temporal categories: ada (performance in its proper time) and qada (makeup after its time). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that the time of ada ends at fajr, as stated in Lubab al-Manasik and endorsed by many authorities.

Key Terms
الرمي (ar-ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the three jamarat during Hajj.
وقت الأداء (waqt al-ada'): The prescribed time in which a ritual act must be performed to fulfill its obligation without makeup.
الجنایات (al-jinayat): Violations or deficient actions in Hajj that require a penalty (dam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, until what time does the time of ada (performance) for stoning on the second day of Tashriq last?
A) Until sunset of the same day
B) Until sunrise of the next day
C) Until fajr (dawn) of the next day
D) Until noon of the next day

Key Takeaway
The time of ada for rami on the second and third days ends at fajr (Imam Abu Hanifa), and stoning after that is qada requiring a dam.

The Order of Stoning the Jamarat: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tartib of jamarat: wajib vs sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the order of stoning the jamarat and distinguish between the sunnah and wajib views, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The order of stoning the jamarat is sunnah, not wajib, in the preferred Hanafi view.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning the order (tartib) of stoning the three jamarat during Hajj. The Prophet's action establishes a sequence, but scholars differ on its legal weight—obligatory (wajib) or recommended (sunnah). We will explore both positions, the evidence cited, and the practical consequences for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the disputed ruling: whether the order of stoning the three jamarat is wajib or sunnah. Note that both positions exist within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the evidence for each position
For the sunnah view: each jamrah is an independent act; the Prophet's action does not imply obligation. For the wajib view: the Prophet always observed order and uncertainty about pebbles implies obligation.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If one stones out of order and does not repeat, the sunnah view holds the rami valid (no dam), while the wajib view requires repetition or a dam.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon position is sunnah (al-Muhit, al-Bahr al-Raiq). The author considers it 'al-mukhtar'. Later scholars like al-Fath confirm.

ولو كن ثلاثاً أعاد على كل جمرة واحدة، ولو كانت حصاة أو حصاتين أعاد كل واحدة ويجزئه لأنه رمى كل واحدة بأكثرها فوقع معتداً به ولكن لم يقع مسنوناً ا ا هـ. ما في المحيط وهو صريح في الخلاف وفي اختيار السنية واعتمده المحقق ابن... من قوله : (فظهر بهذا الخ قال في اللباب : وبغروب الشمس من هذا اليوم أي الرابع يفوت وقت الأداء والقضاء بخلاف ما قبله ولو لم يرم يوم النحر أو الثاني أو الثالث رماه في الليلة المقبلة أي الآتية لكل من الأيام الماضية ولا شيء عليه سوى الإساءة إن لم يكن بعذر، ولو رمى ليلة الحادي عشر عن غدها لم يصح لأن الليالي في الحج في حكم الأيام الماضية لا المستقبلة أي فيجوز رمي يوم الثاني من أيام النحر ليلة الثالثة ولا يجوز فيها رمي يوم الثالث، ولو لم يرم في الليل رماه في النهار قضاء وعليه الكفارة. ولو أخر رمي الأيام كلها إلى الرابع مثلاً قضاها كلها فيه وعليه الجزاء، وإن لم يقض حتى غربت الشمس منه أي من الرابع فات وقت القضاء وليست هذه الليلة أي ليلة الرابع عشر تابعة لما قبلها ليبقي وقت الرمي فيها بخلاف الليالي التي قبلها اهـ. موضحاً من شرحه . والحاصل أنه لو أخر الرمي في غير اليوم الرابع ولم يرم سقط الرمي ولزمه دم قوله: (فلم يجز رمي الأخريين) أي بناء على وجوب الترتيب، وهذا مقابل للقول بالسنية المشار إليه بقوله ليكون إتيانه على الوجه المسنون ولذا عبر بقوله وعن محمد ليدل على أنه قول آخر فتدبر قوله: (وفي اختيار (السنة قال في النهر : هذا سهو بل اختيار التعيين. نعم قال في الفتح : الذي يقع
And he benefited by his saying 'beginning' to the end [indicating] the order between the three jamarat, which is established from his action ﷺ, and he did not clarify whether it is obligatory or sunnah, and there is ikhtilaf therein. In al-Zahiriyya: If one changes this order and on the second day begins with Jamrat al-Aqaba, stones it, then the middle, then the one nearest to Masjid al-Khayf in Mina—and he is still—he repeats the middle jamrah and Jamrat al-Aqaba to come in the sunnah order. In al-Muhit, it is justified that the order is sunnah. He said: 'If he does not repeat, it suffices him because stoning each jamrah is a complete act of worship in itself and is not dependent on others, so its validity is not tied to precedence, like tawaf before rami—it occurs as sunnah.' For example, if one completes the first with four, then repeats the middle with seven, then the Aqaba, he stoned from the first the minimum, and the minimum does not stand for the whole, so it is disregarded, as if he stoned them before the first, so he repeats them. If one stones each with four, he completes each with three, because he stoned the majority of the first, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so as if he stoned the second and third after the first. Starting anew is better to be in the sunnah manner. From Muhammad: If one stones the three jamarat and finds he has four pebbles in his hand, not knowing which they are from, he throws them for the first and then restarts the two remaining, due to the possibility they were from the first, so the latter two are not valid. If there are three, he repeats one for each jamrah. If one or two pebbles, he repeats each one and it suffices him because he stoned each with its majority, so it is valid but not sunnah. End quote from al-Muhit, which is explicit about the ikhtilaf and that the chosen view is sunnah, and the scholar Ibn... confirmed it. From his saying: (Thus it appears) He said in al-Lubab: 'With sunset of this day, i.e., the fourth, the time of ada and qada expires, unlike before. If one does not stone on the day of sacrifice, or the second, or the third, he stones it in the following night for each of the past days, and nothing is due except disapproval (isa'a) if there is no excuse. If one stones on the night of the eleventh for the next day, it is not valid, because nights in Hajj are in the ruling of past days, not future. So it is permissible to stone for the second day on the night of the third, but not for the third on that night. If he does not stone at night, he stones in the daytime as qada and a penalty is due. If he delays all stoning to the fourth, for example, he makes them up all in it and a penalty is due. If he does not make them up until the sun sets on the fourth, the time of qada expires, and this night, i.e., the night of the fourteenth, is not attached to what preceded to keep the time of stoning in it, unlike the preceding nights.' Clarified from his commentary. The summary: If one delays rami on other than the fourth, he stones in the following night of that delayed day, and it is ada because it is attached to it, and nothing is due except isa'a for leaving the sunnah. If he delays to the next day, it is qada and a dam is due. Similarly, if he delays all to the fourth, then when the sun sets on the fourth without stoning, the rami drops and a dam is due. His saying: (then the latter two are not valid) is based on the obligation of order. This is contrasted with the sunnah view referred to by his saying 'to be in the sunnah manner', hence he expressed 'from Muhammad' to indicate it is another opinion. Consider his saying: (and in choice of the sunnah) Al-Nahr said: 'This is a mistake; rather the choice is of specification.' Yes, al-Fath said: 'What occurs...'
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This section from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the order of stoning the three jamarat (tartib). The author notes that the Prophet's practice establishes an order (first the jamrah near the mosque, then the middle, then al-Aqaba), but there is disagreement on whether this order is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah (recommended). The text cites two views: 1) The order is sunnah, as stated in al-Muhit and supported by the reasoning that stoning each jamrah is an independent worship; if one changes the order, the stoning is still valid but the sunnah is missed. 2) The order is wajib, as implied by the narration from Muhammad that if one has extra pebbles and is uncertain, he must repeat the last two. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq seems to side with the sunnah position, calling it 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen view). The passage also includes detailed scenarios from al-Muhit about how to correct if the stoning is not in order or if the number of pebbles is uncertain. It also touches on the timing rules for qada when stoning is delayed beyond its day, summarizing that if one misses a day, he may stone the following night as ada (if same day's night) or the next day as qada (with dam). The key point is that the order is sunnah, so missing it does not invalidate but may require repeating if one wishes to achieve the sunnah. The mufta bihi is that it is sunnah, as confirmed by later scholars like al-Fath.

Key Terms
الترتيب (at-tartib): The prescribed order of stoning the jamarat: first the one nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then Jamrat al-Aqaba.
مسنون (masnun): A recommended act (sunnah) established by the Prophet's practice, not obligatory.
الإناءة (al-isa'a): Disapproval (makruh) for leaving a sunnah without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the order of stoning the three jamarat?
A) It is wajib; missing it requires a dam.
B) It is sunnah; missing it does not invalidate.
C) It is fard; missing it invalidates the Hajj.
D) It is makruh to follow it.

Key Takeaway
The order of stoning the jamarat is sunnah in the preferred Hanafi view; stoning out of sequence is valid but not optimal.

Rulings on Stoning (Rami) in Hajj: Order and Timing
Commentary on stoning rulings with two intra-madhhab disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of stoning the three Jamarat, identify the mufta bihi position, and explain the dispute regarding stoning on the fourth day before zawal.

Core Idea
The order of stoning is sunnah, not wajib, in the relied-upon Hanafi position; stoning on the fourth day before noon is valid but makruh according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two key issues in the ritual of stoning the Jamarat: whether the order of stoning the three pillars is obligatory or recommended, and the permissibility of stoning on the fourth day before noon. These issues involve intra-madhhab disagreement and require careful understanding of the evidence and the tarjih mechanism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses (1) the legal nature of the order (tarib) of stoning the three Jamarat, and (2) the ruling on stoning on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah) before zawal. Note that the order is established from the Prophet's action but its binding force is disputed.
The order is between the small (Ula), middle (Wusta), and large (Aqaba) Jamarat.
2
Analyse the order dispute
For the order, the commentatory reports that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it sunnah, while Muhammad has a narration deeming it wajib. Examine the evidence: the order is sunnah because each Jamarah is an independent act of worship; violating it does not invalidate the stoning, as per al-Muhit. Muhammad's view relies on the necessity of following the Prophet's sequence.
The tarjih (preferred view) is that the order is sunnah, as stated by al-Kasani, al-Muhit, and Fatawa al-Sirajiyya.
3
Examine the fourth day timing dispute
Abu Hanifa permits stoning before zawal on the 13th, based on a narration from Ibn Abbas and qiyas on the permissibility of leaving early from Mina. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize to other days where stoning before noon is not allowed. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: valid but makruh under Abu Hanifa; invalid and requiring repetition under Sahibayn.
The mufta bihi among later authorities is the Sahibayn's view, but Abu Hanifa's position is known and may be followed.
4
Apply the rulings
Given a scenario where a pilgrim stones the middle Jamarah before the small one on the 11th, state the Hanafi ruling: the stoning is valid but not in the best manner; no repetition is required. For stoning on the 13th before noon, under the mufta bihi, it would be invalid and must be repeated after zawal.
The passage also covers other scenarios like incomplete stones, but focus on these two core issues.

Book of Hajj – Chapter of Ihram. Stoning: due to the expiry of its time, and upon him one dam (sacrifice) by agreement. If it was the day of his stoning, and if it was with seven because so it appears from this that for stoning there is a time of performance and a time of make-up. And he benefited by his saying 'beginning to end' to the order among the three Jamarat, which is established from his action (peace be upon him) and he did not clarify whether it is obligatory or sunnah, and there is disagreement in it. In al-Zahiriyya: if he changed this order and began on the second day with Jamrat al-Aqaba and stoned it, then the middle, then the one that is next to the Mosque of al-Khayf in Mina, and he is still afterward, he repeats the middle Jamarah and Jamrat al-Aqaba to perform them in order as a sunnah. And it was reasoned in al-Muhit that the order is sunnah. He said: If he does not repeat, it suffices him, because stoning each Jamarah is a complete act of worship in itself and is not subsidiary to some, so its permissibility is not dependent on the precedence of some over others, like tawaf before stoning occurs as a sunnah. Then he detailed cases of incomplete stones. And from Muhammad: if he stoned the three Jamarat and in his hand are four pebbles, not knowing which one they are from, he throws them for the first (Jamarah) and begins the remaining two Jamarat fresh because it is possible that they are from the first, so the stoning of the last two is not valid... And it is clear in the disagreement and in choosing the sunnah, and the verifying scholar Ibn...
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the rulings of stoning (rami) during Hajj. It begins by establishing that stoning has two time categories: the time for performance (ada) and the time for make-up (qada). The author then discusses the order (tarib) of stoning the three Jamarat (Ula, Wusta, and Aqaba). The order is established by the Prophet's practice but there is ikhtilaf on whether it is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah (recommended). The commentary reports from al-Zahiriyya and al-Muhit that the order is sunnah, meaning that violating it does not require repetition but it is better to repeat for the sunnah. Detailed scenarios are given: if one stoned the first Jamarah with four stones and then repeated the middle with seven, etc., the ruling depends on whether the minimum count was fulfilled. The commentary then moves to the timing of stoning: if one delays stoning on the first three days (10th, 11th, 12th), they can stone at night of the following day as ada, but if they delay to the fourth day (13th), stoning becomes qada and a dam is required. If sunset of the 13th passes without stoning, the obligation drops and a dam is due. The passage also covers the dispute among Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding stoning on the fourth day before zawal (noon). Abu Hanifa permits it as makruh, while the Sahibayn prohibit it by analogy with other days. The author supports the view that the order is sunnah, citing multiple sources including al-Muhit and al-Lubab. Finally, the passage lists recommended acts during stoning: making du'a, raising hands with palms facing the sky, facing the Qibla, etc., and notes that women and the sick are excused if they miss stoning due to crowd or illness.

Key Terms
رمي (rami): The ritual stoning of the Jamarat (stone pillars) during Hajj.
ترتيب (tarib): The prescribed order of stoning the three Jamarat: first the small (Ula), then the middle (Wusta), then the large (Aqaba).
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; omission does not invalidate the ritual but is contrary to the preferred practice.
قضاء (qada): Make-up for a missed wajib act; if stoning is delayed beyond its ada time, it becomes qada and a dam is required.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for omitting a wajib act in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling on the order (tarib) of stoning the three Jamarat?
A) It is wajib; if violated the stoning is invalid.
B) It is sunnah; violation does not require repetition but is disliked.
C) It is haram to change the order.
D) It is fard; one must repeat the entire stoning.

Key Takeaway
Stoning the Jamarat is wajib, but the order is sunnah; stoning on the fourth day before zawal is invalid according to the mufta bihi, so pilgrims should stone after noon.

Walking vs. Riding for Ramy: The Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ramy method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the preferred method of ramy (walking vs. riding) and explain which position is mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
Walking for ramy shows humility, but riding may follow the Prophet's teaching action.

Ramy is a key Hajj ritual, but how should one perform it—walking or riding? The early Hanafi imams differed on this point. This lesson explores the three opinions, the evidence for each, and the preferred view according to Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the opinions of Abu Hanifa & Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and the preferred view in Fath al-Qadir.
Note that the third opinion is a refinement of Abu Yusuf's view.
2
Understand the dalil for each
What reasoning supports each position? Consider humility, following the Prophet's example, and practical concerns.
3
Analyze the tarjih
Why does Fath al-Qadir prefer walking except for Jamrat al-Aqaba on the last day? Examine the arguments for humility and harm avoidance.
The Prophet's riding was for teaching, not necessarily for preference.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
How does this difference affect a pilgrim's practice? Determine when to walk and when to ride based on the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سألت إبراهيم أيما أفضل للحاج أن يرمي راجلاً أو راكباً؟ فقلت راجلاً. فخطأني ثم قلت: راكباً فخطأني ثم قال: ما كان يوقف عندها فالأفضل أن يرميها راجلاً. وما لا يوقف عندها فالأفضل أن يرميها راكباً. قال: فخرجت من عنده فما بلغت الباب حتى سمعت صراخ النساء أنه قد توفي إلى رحمة الله تعالى، فلو كان شيء أفضل من مذاكرة العلم لاشتغل به في هذه الحالة لأن هذه الحالة حالة الندامة والحسرة ا هـ . وأما قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد فعلى ما في فتاوی قاضیخان أن الرمي كله راكباً أفضل في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وعلى ما في فتاوى الظهيرية أن الرمي كله ماشياً أفضل فإن ركب إليها فلا بأس به يعني عندهما لأنه حكى قول أبي يوسف بعده، فتحصل أن في هذه المسألة ثلاثة أقوال رجح في فتح القدير ما في الظهيرية لأن أداءها ماشياً أقرب إلى التواضع والخشوع وخصوصاً في هذا الزمان فإن عامة المسلمين في جميع الرمي فلا يؤمن من الأذى بالركوب بينهم بالزحمة. ورميه عليه السلام راكباً إنما هو ليظهر فعله ليقتدي به كطوافه راكباً .ا.هـ. ولو قيل بأنه ماشياً أفضل إلا في رمي جمرة العقبة في اليوم الأخير فهو راكباً أفضل لكان له وجه باعتبار أنه ذاهب إلى مكة في هذه الساعة كما هو العادة وغالب الناس راكب فلا إيذاء في ركوبه مع تحصيل فضيلة الاتباع له
I asked Ibrahim: 'What is better for the pilgrim: to stone walking or riding?' I said: 'Walking.' He corrected me. Then I said: 'Riding.' He corrected me. Then he said: 'For those (jamarat) where one stands, it is better to stone walking. For those where one does not stand, it is better to stone riding.' He said: 'I left him and had hardly reached the door when I heard the women screaming that he had died to the mercy of Allah. If there were anything better than discussing knowledge, he would have occupied himself with it in that state, because that state is a state of regret and sorrow.' End quote. As for the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, according to Fatawa Qadikhan, all stoning is better riding in the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, all stoning is better walking, and if one rides to it, there is no harm, meaning in their view, because he narrated the saying of Abu Yusuf after it. So it becomes clear that there are three sayings in this issue. In Fath al-Qadir, he preferred what is in al-Zahiriyyah because performing it walking is closer to humility and reverence, especially in this time, since the generality of Muslims are walking in all the stoning, and riding among them in the crowd may not be safe from harm. And the Prophet's stoning while riding was only to show his action so that people would follow him, like his tawaf while riding. End quote. If it were said that walking is better except for stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba on the last day, then riding is better, it would have a face, considering that he is going to Makkah at that hour, as is the custom and most people ride, so there is no harm in his riding while attaining the virtue of following him.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the preferred method of performing the stoning ritual (ramy) during Hajj. It begins with a narrative about Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i) who clarifies that for jamarat where pilgrims stand (i.e., the first and second jamarat), walking is better; for the one where they do not stand (Jamrat al-Aqaba), riding is better. The author then reports the positions of the early Hanafi imams: according to Fatawa Qadikhan, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that all stoning is better while riding; according to Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, all stoning is better while walking, with no harm if one rides (this view is attributed to Abu Yusuf). Thus three opinions exist. The author of Fath al-Qadir preferred the walking view because it displays humility and avoids harm in crowds, noting that the Prophet's riding was only to teach, not because it was better in every circumstance. A further refinement suggests walking is generally better except for Jamrat al-Aqaba on the last day, when riding is better because the pilgrim is heading to Makkah with most people riding, so there is no harm and one can follow the Prophet's example. The passage ends by considering this view as plausible.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): Stoning the jamarat (pillars) at Mina during Hajj
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The large pillar denoting the devil's temptation of Prophet Ibrahim, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and subsequent days

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Fath al-Qadir, when is it better to perform ramy riding?
A) For all jamarat
B) Only for Jamrat al-Aqaba on the last day
C) Never
D) Only for the first two jamarat

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view is to walk for ramy except on the last day for Jamrat al-Aqaba, where riding is better.

Sending Luggage Ahead to Makkah While at Mina
Ruling on sending luggage ahead to Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sending luggage ahead to Makkah while staying at Mina and identify the condition that removes the dislikedness.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead is disliked due to heart distraction; if safe, no karahah.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hajj: the permissibility of sending one's heavy luggage to Makkah while the pilgrim remains at Mina to perform the stoning. The Hanafi school considers this act disliked (makruh) unless the luggage is secure, based on a Companion's statement and the principle of avoiding distraction in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is sending one's thaqal (heavy baggage) ahead to Makkah while staying at Mina for ramy. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh).
The karahah is tanzihiyyah (not sinful).
2
Locate the Dalil
The first proof is an athar from Ibn Umar via Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'Whoever sends his thaqal before the departure, he has no Hajj.' The second is qiyas: it distracts the heart from worship.
The athar is a saying of a Companion, not a prophetic hadith.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The phrase 'no Hajj for him' is interpreted as negation of perfection (nafy al-kamal), not validity. The distraction argument supports karahah, not prohibition.
The literal interpretation would contradict other texts; thus it is figurative.
4
Note the Condition
The dislikedness applies only when the luggage is not secure in Makkah. If it is safe, there is no heart distraction, so no karahah.
Security removes the cause of dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويكره أن تقدم ثقلك إلى مكة وتقيم بمنى للرمي لأثر ابن أبي شيبة عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنه من قدم ثقله قبل النفر فلا حج له وأراد نفي الكمال ولأنه يوجب شغل قلبه وهو في العبادة فيكره والظاهر أنها تنزيهية والثَّقَل متاع المسافر وحشمه وهو بفتحتين وجمعه أثقال. وأشار إلى أنه يكره ترك أمتعته بمكة والذهاب إلى عرفات بالطريق الأولى لأنها العبادة المقصودة بخلاف الرمي وينبغي أن يكون محل الكراهة في المسألتين عند عدم الأمن عليها بمكة أما أن أمن فلا لعدم شغل القلب
His saying: (And it is disliked that you send your thaqal ahead to Makkah and you stay at Mina for the stoning) due to the athar of Ibn Abi Shaybah from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Whoever sends his thaqal before the departure, he has no Hajj' — and he meant negation of perfection. And because it causes his heart to be occupied while he is in worship, so it is disliked. And it appears that the dislikedness is of the tanzih type. And ath-thaqal is the traveler's belongings and retinue; it is with two fathahs, and its plural is athqal. And he indicated that it is disliked to leave his belongings in Makkah and go to Arafat in a primary way, because that is the intended worship unlike ramy. And the place of dislikedness in both matters should be when there is no security over them in Makkah; if there is security, then no dislikedness due to lack of heart occupation.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states that it is makruh for a pilgrim to send his heavy luggage (thaqal) ahead to Makkah while he himself stays at Mina to perform ramy. The author provides two proofs: first, an athar from Ibn Umar via Ibn Abi Shaybah saying that one who sends his thaqal before the departure (nafr) has no Hajj — interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity. Second, the act distracts the heart from worship, leading to karahah. The author clarifies that the karahah is tanzihiyyah (disliked but not sinful). The term thaqal refers to the traveler's belongings and servants. By extension, it is even more disliked to leave belongings in Makkah and go to Arafat because Arafat is the essential worship. The exception is if the belongings are safe; then no distraction exists, so no karahah.

Key Terms
ثقل (thaqal): The traveler's heavy baggage and retinue
تنزيهية (tanzihiyyah): Disliked but not sinful; recommended to avoid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What removes the dislikedness of sending one's luggage ahead to Makkah?
A) If one stays at Mina
B) If the luggage is safe and one's heart is not occupied
C) If one intends to perform Hajj tamattu'
D) If one is a Makkan resident

Key Takeaway
Sending thaqal to Makkah while at Mina is makruh tanzih when not secure; if secure, it is not disliked.

The Sunnah of Staying at al-Muhassab (النزول بالمحصب)
Fiqh ruling on a recommended post-ramy practice, with a digression on hand positions and legal grading.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of staying at al-Muhassab after ramy and explain the basis for its sunnah status, including the related digression on hand positions and the nature of karahah.

Core Idea
Staying at al-Muhassab is a sunnah because the Prophet did so to demonstrate Allah's victory over the disbelievers who conspired there.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a recommended practice (sunnah) for pilgrims after completing the stoning ritual. The Prophet alighted at al-Muhassab, a place between Mina and Makkah, to display Allah's subtle victory over the disbelievers. Understanding this ruling helps us see how prophetic actions become established as sunnah, and also introduces a related debate on hand positions in du'a and the spectrum of legal dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is staying at al-Muhassab after ramy. The text states it is a sunnah. Determine that sunnah is a recommended practice; omission is not sinful but blameworthy.
The term 'sunnah' here is used in the Hanafi sense: an act that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Understand the Basis (Dalil)
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is the primary evidence. He alighted at al-Muhassab specifically because the disbelievers had conspired there, and he wanted to show them Allah's power.
This is an example of a non-obligatory act becoming sunnah through continuous practice (al-muwazabah).
3
Note the Analogy (Tashbih)
The text compares it to raml (quick walking) in tawaf, which is also a sunnah. This suggests that staying at al-Muhassab is a recommended but not obligatory act.
Raml is a sunnah of tawaf; similarly, staying at al-Muhassab is a sunnah of the hajj after ramy.
4
Examine the Digression on Hand Positions in Du'a
The commentary quotes a dispute: some say during du'a one should face the palms toward the Ka'bah, others say raise hands to shoulders. The author mentions that Qadikhan chose the first view.
This is a secondary issue; the main lesson remains on al-Muhassab.
5
Analyze the Karahah Dispute
The text discusses whether the dislikedness (karahah) of leaving the sunnah is tanzihi (slightly disliked) or tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The author mentions a reflection on Umar's discipline, suggesting it might be tahrimi, but the teacher dismisses that, saying Umar disciplined for leaving the better.
This shows the Hanafi precision in grading repugnance: tanzihi vs tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم إلى المحَصَب) أي ثم رح إليه وهو بضم الميم وفتح المهملتين وهو الأبطح موضع ذات حصى بين منى ومكة وليست المقبرة منه وكانت الكفار اجتمعوا فيه وتحالفوا على إضرار رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنزل عليه السلام فيه إراءة لهم لطيف صنع الله به وتكريمه بنصرته فصار ذلك سنة كالرمل في الطواف. وعبارة المجمع يجعل باطن كفيه نحو الكعبة كما في السراج وقال الثاني: يرفع يديه حذاء منكبيه كما في سائر الأدعية واقتصر عليه في النحر ا.هـ. قال في شرح اللباب واختاره قاضيخان وغيره والظاهر الأول قوله : (والظاهر أنها تنزيهية نظر فيه في النهر بأن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه كان يمنع منه ويؤدب عليه قال: وهذا يؤذن بأنها تحريمية إذ لا يؤدب على التنزيهية ا هـ. قال شيخنا فيه نظر فإنه: رضي الله تعالى عنه كان يؤدب على ترك خلاف الأولى. هذا وفي السراج: وكذا يكره للإنسان أن يجعل شيئاً من حوائجه خلفه ويصلي مثل النعل وشبهه لأنه يشغل خاطره فلا يتفرغ للعبادة على
His saying: (Then to al-Muhassab) meaning then proceed to it. It is with dammah on the meem and fatha on the haa and saad. It is al-Abtah, a place with pebbles between Mina and Makkah, and the cemetery is not part of it. The disbelievers gathered there and conspired to harm the Messenger of Allah, so he alighted there to show them the subtlety of Allah's dealing with him and honoring him with victory. Thus it became a sunnah like raml in tawaf. The expression of al-Majma': he places the inside of his palms towards the Ka'bah as in al-Siraj; and the second said: he raises his hands to his shoulders as in other supplications, and he limited himself to that in al-Nahr. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: and Qadikhan and others chose it, and the apparent is the first. His saying: (and it appears that it is tanzihi) he reflected on it in al-Nahr because Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, used to prevent it and discipline for it. He said: this indicates it is tahrimi, because one does not discipline for tanzihi. End quote. Our teacher said: there is reflection in it, for he, may Allah be pleased with him, used to discipline for leaving what is contrary to the first. This and in al-Siraj: likewise it is disliked for a person to place any of his needs behind him and pray, like a sandal and the like, because it disturbs his mind so he is not free for worship.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage describes the sunnah of going to al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah), a pebbly place between Mina and Makkah. The Prophet alighted there because it was where the disbelievers conspired against him, and Allah gave him victory. It became a sunnah, similar to raml (quick walking) in tawaf. The text then digresses into a discussion about hand positions during du'a, which is not directly related to the main topic. The author then quotes a dispute about whether the karahah (dislike) mentioned earlier is tanzihi or tahrimi, noting that Umar used to discipline for it, which suggests tahrimi, but the author's teacher argues that Umar disciplined for leaving the better, not for a sin. The passage ends with a related ruling: it is disliked to place objects (like sandals) behind oneself while praying because it distracts the mind.

Key Terms
المحصب (al-Muhassab): A place with pebbles between Mina and Makkah, also called al-Abtah
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice established by the Prophet's action
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Light dislike; omission is not sinful but better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To rest before entering Makkah
B) To show the disbelievers Allah's victory and power
C) To pray in a specific manner
D) To meet the Ansar

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's action of staying at al-Muhassab after ramy establishes it as a sunnah; its omission is lightly disliked but does not invalidate Hajj.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Obligation, Dispute, and Times
Ruling on Tawaf al-Sadr with dispute and time rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Tawaf al-Sadr, explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school over the meaning of 'sadr', and identify the two time frames for performing it.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all except Makkans; dispute is whether 'sadr' means return from Hajj or to family.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses Tawaf al-Sadr, its names, obligation, and a key dispute with the Shafi'i school. The Hanafis rule that staying after performing it does not invalidate the tawaf, while the Shafi'is require immediate departure. The text also explains the permissible and recommended times for this tawaf and the rules if one misses it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the people of Makkah. The term 'sadr' means return from the actions of Hajj.
The obligation is based on a hadith from Sahih Muslim.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that 'sadr' means return to one's family, so the tawaf must be performed as the very last action before departing to one's home.
This difference arises from the interpretation of the word 'sadr'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school argues that the tawaf is invalid if one stays after performing it, because the departure (to family) is the intended context.
No explicit dalil is given in the text; the dispute is over linguistic meaning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the addition 'for al-sadr' indicates specification: the departure is either the cause or condition of the ruling, both of which precede the ruling. The Shafi'i view would make the departure subsequent, which is illogical.
This is a linguistic and logical argument.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one performs Tawaf al-Sadr and then stays in Makkah, according to Hanafis the tawaf remains valid; according to Shafi'is it must be repeated.
The Hanafi view is considered correct by the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فطف للصدر سبعة أشواط وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة وله خمسة أسام ما في الكتاب لأنه يصدر عنه أي يرجع والصدر الرجوع، وطواف الوداع لأنه يودع البيت به، وطواف الإفاضة لأنه لأجله يفيض إلى البيت من منى وطواف آخر عهد بالبيت لأنه لا طواف بعده وطواف الواجب واختلف في المراد بالصدر الذي هو الرجوع فعندنا هو الرجوع عن أفعال الحج، وعند الشافعي هو الرجوع إلى أهله ويبتنى عليه أنه لو طاف للصدر ثم أقام بمكة لشغل لم تلزمه الإعادة عندنا خلافاً له، والصحيح قولنا لأن الإضافة للاختصاص وهو إما باعتبار أن الصدر سبب أو شرط وكل منهما سابق على الحكم وهو بما قلنا، وعلى قوله يكون متأخراً عن الحكم والفراغ عن الأفعال صدوراً ورجوعاً عنها يسمى إلى الحالة التي كانت من قبل. ولم يبين وقته وله وقتان وقت الجواز ووقت الاستحباب؛ فالأول أوله بعد طواف الزيادة إذا كان على عزم السفر حتى لو طاف كذلك ثم أطال الإقامة بمكة وله سنة ولم ينو الإقامة بها ولم يتخذها داراً جاز طوافه وأما آخره فليس بموقت ما دام مقيماً حتى لو أقام عاماً لا ينوي الإقامة فله أن يطوف ويقع أداء، والثاني أن يوقعه عند إرادة السفر حتى روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه لو طافه ثم أقام إلى العشاء فأحب إلى أن يطوف طوافاً آخر ليكون توديع البيت آخر مورده كذا في المحيط . ولم يشترط المصنف له نية معينة فأفاد أنه لو طاف بعد ما حل النفر ونوى التطوع أجزأه عن الصدر كما لو طاف بنية التطوع في أيام النحر وقع عن الفرض. وأفاد ببيان صفته أنه لو نفر ولم يطف يجب عليه أن يرجع فيطوفه لكن قالوا: ما لم يجاوز المواقيت فإن جاوزها لم يجب الرجوع عيناً بل إما أن يمضي وعليه دم، وإما أن يرجع فيرجع بإحرام جديد لأن الميقات لا يجاوز بلا إحرام فيحرم بعمرة، فإذا رجع ابتدأ بطواف العمرة ثم يطوف للصدر ولا شيء عليه لتأخيره وقالوا: الأولى أن لا يرجع ويريق دماً لأنه أنفع للفقراء وأيسر عليه لما فيه من دفع ضرر التزام الإحرام ومشقة الطريق. والدليل على وجوبه من السنة أحاديث أصرحها ما في صحيح مسلم: كانوا ينصرفون في كل وجه فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا ينصرفن أحد حتى يكون آخر عهده بالبيت . وأراد بأهل مكة من اتخذ مكة أو داخل المواقيت داراً فلا طواف صدر على من كان داخل
His saying: (So perform tawaf for al-sadr seven circuits, and it is wajib except for the people of Makkah.) It has five names mentioned in the book: because one departs (yasdur) by it, i.e., returns; al-sadr means return; Tawaf al-Wada' because one bids farewell to the House with it; Tawaf al-Ifadah because for it one flows (yufid) from Mina to the House; Tawaf Akhir 'Ahd bi'l-Bayt because there is no tawaf after it; and Tawaf al-Wajib. There is a difference in the meaning of al-sadr which is 'return': according to us it is the return from the actions of Hajj; according to al-Shafi'i it is the return to one's family. Upon this is built that if one performs tawaf al-sadr and then stays in Makkah for some need, repetition is not necessary according to us, contrary to him. The correct is our view because the addition is for specification, and it is either because al-sadr is the cause or condition, and each is antecedent to the ruling, and it is as we said. According to his view, it would be subsequent to the ruling and the completion of actions, called 'return' to the previous state. And he did not specify its time. It has two times: a time of permissibility and a time of recommendation. The first: its beginning is after Tawaf al-Ziyadah if one has the intention of travel, such that if one performs tawaf thus and then prolongs his stay in Makkah for a year without intending residence and without taking it as a home, his tawaf is valid. As for its end, it is not time-bound as long as he is staying; even if he stays a year without intending residence, he may perform tawaf and it counts as performance. The second: that he performs it when he intends to travel; it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that if he performed it and then stayed until evening, he prefers that he perform another tawaf so that bidding farewell to the House is his final action, as in al-Muhit. The author did not require a specific intention for it, so it indicates that if he performed tawaf after halal al-nafr and intended supererogatory, it suffices for tawaf al-sadr, just as if he performed supererogatory tawaf during the days of Nahr, it counts for the obligatory. And it indicates in explaining its description that if he departs without performing tawaf, he must return to perform it, but they said: as long as he has not passed the miqat. If he has passed it, return is not required in person; rather either he continues and upon him is a dam, or he returns and he returns with a new ihram because the miqat cannot be crossed without ihram, so he assumes ihram for 'umrah. When he returns he begins with tawaf of 'umrah, then performs tawaf al-sadr, and nothing is upon him for its delay. And they said: it is better that he does not return and gives a dam, because it is more beneficial for the poor and easier for him, due to avoiding the harm of adhering to ihram and the hardship of the road. The evidence for its obligation from the Sunnah is the most explicit of the hadiths: what is in Sahih Muslim: 'They were departing in every direction, so the Messenger of Allah said: None of you should depart until his last action is the tawaf of the House.' And by 'people of Makkah' he meant those who have taken Makkah or within the miqat as a home, so there is no tawaf al-sadr on those who are inside (the miqat).
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about Tawaf al-Sadr (the farewell circumambulation). The author states that it is wajib (obligatory) for pilgrims except the people of Makkah. It has five names: Tawaf al-Sadr, Tawaf al-Wada', Tawaf al-Ifadah, Tawaf Akhir 'Ahd, and Tawaf al-Wajib. The key point of dispute is the meaning of 'sadr' (return). The Hanafis hold that it means returning from the actions of Hajj (i.e., the farewell tawaf is tied to completing Hajj rituals). The Shafi'is hold it means returning to one's family. The practical consequence: if one performs Tawaf al-Sadr and then stays in Makkah for a need, according to Hanafis, repetition is not required; according to Shafi'is, the tawaf would be invalidated because it is meant to be the very last act before departing to one's family. The Hanafis argue that the addition 'for al-sadr' indicates specification: the departure is either the cause or condition of the tawaf, both of which precede the ruling. The Shafi'i view would make the departure subsequent to the tawaf, which is illogical. The passage then discusses the time of the tawaf: it has a time of permissibility (after Tawaf al-Ziyadah if intending travel, and it remains valid even if the stay is prolonged) and a time of recommendation (when actually about to depart). If one misses the tawaf and has already left, he must return if he has not passed the miqat; if he has passed, he may either pay a dam (blood) or return with a new ihram for 'umrah, but the preferred option is to pay the dam as it is easier and more beneficial for the poor. The proof from Sahih Muslim is cited: the Prophet said, 'None of you should depart until his last action is the tawaf of the House.' Finally, the exemption for the people of Makkah is defined: those who have made Makkah or the area within the miqat their home.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed after completing Hajj rituals before leaving Makkah
صدر (sadr): Return; in context, return from Hajj actions
أهل مكة (ahl Makkah): Those who have made Makkah or within the miqat their home

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim performs Tawaf al-Sadr but then stays in Makkah for a few days due to necessity, what is the ruling?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
B) The tawaf is valid and does not need repetition
C) He must sacrifice a dam
D) He must perform an additional 'umrah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all except Makkans; the Hanafi interpretation of 'sadr' as return from Hajj actions allows pilgrims to stay after performing it without repetition.

Tawaf as-Sadr: Ruling, Proof, and Exceptions
Expands on the ruling and exceptions of tawaf as-sadr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the farewell tawaf, identify its proof from the Sunnah, and apply the exceptions for residents and those with excuses.

Core Idea
The farewell tawaf is wajib from ahad hadith; three exceptions exempt it: residency, missing Hajj, and valid excuses.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of tawaf as-sadr, the farewell tawaf. We will explore its obligation as wajib (not fard), the proof from the hadith in Sahih Muslim, the exceptions for residents of Makkah and those within the mawaqit, and the timing and consequences of missing it. We also examine the inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding the meaning of 'sadr' and an intra-Hanafi difference on when residency waives the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, understand what the farewell tawaf is and its legal classification. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory) except for the people of Makkah and those within the mawaqit. The passage lists five names for this tawaf, each highlighting a different aspect.
Wajib here means a binding obligation that is established by zanni evidence; it is not fard (based on qati' evidence).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith in Sahih Muslim: 'Let none of you depart until his last affair with the House (be the tawaf).' This is an ahad hadith, which in Hanafi usul yields zanni thubut and thus wajib, not fard.
The hadith is a prohibition (nahi) of departing without tawaf; the Hanafis interpret this as a command to perform the tawaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The specific phrase 'آخر عهده بالبيت' indicates that the tawaf must be the final act before departure. The negative imperative 'لا ينصرفن' emphasizes that it is not permissible to leave without it.
Hanafi usul considers that a nahi (prohibition) indicates tahrim (prohibition of leaving without tawaf), which translates to a command to perform it.
4
Identify the exceptions
The text specifies several categories who are exempt: (1) residents of Makkah and those living inside the mawaqit, (2) a person performing 'umra (only for Hajj), (3) someone who missed the Hajj (faa'it), (4) menstruating and postpartum women due to excuse. However, if a woman becomes pure before leaving, she must perform it.
The exemption for menstruating women is not mentioned explicitly in this passage but is derived from the general rule that excuses drop obligations.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion regarding an afaqi (outsider) who intends to reside in Makkah after the first departure (an-nafr al-awwal). Abu Hanifa says the farewell tawaf is not waived, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (according to one report) say it is waived. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq considers the apparent position (al-zaahir) to be the absolute view, likely following Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the tawaf is not waived in this case.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf with Shafi'i
The disagreement with al-Shafi'i on the meaning of 'sadr' (return from Hajj actions vs. return to family) leads to a practical difference: if a Hanafi performs the tawaf then stays in Makkah, he does not need to repeat it, whereas a Shafi'i must repeat when finally leaving.
The Hanafi view is considered correct because the cause (sadr) precedes the ruling, and the tawaf is tied to completing Hajj acts.
